Jiading 76

Crackdown on Drug Production Operation

Fan Shilin, a native of Wanshan Township, south of Xinmu Bridge outside the East Gate of this county, opened a teahouse in the township, collected commissions for gambling, and also organized a drug production operation to manufacture red pills and traffic them to various places. The rumors have been circulating for many years. Because of his powerful means, he has not been caught. The year before last, he had a dispute with his accomplice, Lu Amao from Baoshan, over a romantic affair. Fan instigated his gang to beat Lu to death and move the body to Baojie. The case has not been solved yet. Lu's wife, Ms. So-and-so, was unwilling to let it go and secretly reported Fan's drug production operation to the Baoshan County Detective Team. On the 21st of this month, Team Leader Wang and more than 30 policemen, accompanied by Lu's wife, took two boats and secretly ambushed near Fan's house. Around 5:00 PM, they surrounded and searched the house. Fan heard the alarm in his sleep, put on his clothes, got up, and opened fire with a pistol, resisting fiercely and trying to escape. However, the pursuers had densely surrounded him, and he was eventually captured. Eighteen packets of red pills and a pistol were seized in his house. Most of his gang members fled. It is now known that the suspect and the seized items have been sent to the Shanghai Garrison Headquarters for interrogation.

Yangzhou 77

Petition to Reduce and Postpone City Land Tax

The land survey in Jiangdu has been completed and the land tax in the urban and rural areas will soon be levied. Local residents, such as Zhu Zhuxuan, feel that the local people are poor and have exhausted their resources. The sudden imposition of this tax is something the people cannot afford. They have jointly submitted a petition to the County Party Department, requesting that it suggest to the County Government to reduce the land tax and postpone the grain levy. The reasons for the petition are: (1) Jiangdu has always been a strategically important place since its history. Whenever there is a military conflict, the markets are reduced to ruins. There has never been a land tax. During the Qianlong period of the Qing Dynasty, the markets were restored, and only rent was paid for the land. The land tax was exempted due to the salt merchants' contribution of huge sums of money. In recent years, with the implementation of land administration, the authorities have proposed to collect grain in the city. It is heard that the households with taxable residential land will be levied, and the collection of grain is indicated on the printed list with the city map. Each mu is levied one qian, four fen, and five li of labor, and five sheng and five he of rice, totaling about two or three yuan. It will be levied in the 24th year, and those who hear about it are indignant and those who talk about it change color. Those who are involved are unable to bear it, and every household cries out, so it is better to jointly appeal. The grain levy is a legacy of the imperial system, the so-called "heavenly grain tribute," which should be exempted with the imperial system. The former Jiangsu Provincial Assembly discussed and requested its abolition because it was related to the national tax, but it could not be done. Now, collecting grain in the city is even worse, which is not allowed by Party rule. Moreover, the military and other miscellaneous offices do not have grain levies. (2) The land tax in Jiangdu should be based on the three grades and nine levels. Whether the regulations for the land tax in the city have been approved by the Legislative Yuan and approved by the Executive Yuan. Moreover, the land in the city has superior and inferior, prosperous and remote areas. Whether they are the same grade is not fair. Even if it is said to be two and a half grades, the people's strength cannot bear it. Moreover, the new salt law will soon be implemented, and the market will decline in the future. There will be demolition but no construction, and it will be difficult to collect taxes. Therefore, it is not enough to reduce taxes to facilitate the implementation. (3) Jiangdu has always relied on the salt industry. Judging from the current situation, it will be difficult to stop the grain levy without exempting it. It should also be postponed, otherwise it will hinder the land reporting. Moreover, the tax rules must be determined after the establishment of autonomy and implemented simultaneously throughout the province. Now that autonomy has not yet been implemented and the counties are not uniform, it cannot be implemented immediately because of the opportunity to report the land of the taxable residences. Therefore, no matter whether the land reporting is done first, or the city land tax is held after the place is prosperous, it can avoid misunderstandings.

Nantong 78

County Government Executes Five Bandits in Jinsha by Firing Squad

Zhang Xiande's home in Jinsha was invaded and robbed by bandits, who also injured the couple. The Security Team arrested five bandits, Wei Qiaosheng, Gu Dehe, Wu Shiyu, Zhu Debiao, and Wang Jinhua. After interrogation by the county government, they confessed their crimes. With the approval of the provincial government, they were escorted to the execution ground in the east of the city on the 23rd and executed by firing squad.

Hangzhou 79

Large Group of Red Bandit Leaders Escorted to Jiangxi

The Zhejiang Security Column, various regiments, and the Nationalist Army's Wu Chengren Division and Wang Yaowu Brigade, etc., captured 35 Red bandit leaders, including fake division and regiment commanders, and more than 1,800 bandit soldiers in Eastern Jiangxi. They were escorted to Hangzhou. After being approved by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek through Yu Jishi, the director of the Zhejiang Security Office, the bandit leaders were transferred to the Nanchang Pacification Headquarters to be handled together with the Fang Zhimin bandit case. The Security Office specifically dispatched soldiers led by a specialist yesterday (23rd) to escort 35 bandit leaders, including Zhou Qun, the head of the pseudo-army group defense bureau, Tan Shiqing, the minister of the pseudo-army group health department, Hu Tiantao, the commander of the pseudo-21st division, Qiu Yucheng, the chief of staff, and Li Shubin, the political commissar of the pseudo-19th division, to Jiangxi by night train at 5:55. The more than 1,800 bandit soldiers are planned to be given moral education in Hangzhou.

Recruiting Disaster Labor to Rebuild the New Line

The Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway is rebuilding a new line to connect with the Qiantang River Bridge, from Jingjiang Station on the riverbank to Xiaoshan, with a length of 12 kilometers and an estimated earthwork of more than 300,000 cubic meters. Zeng Yangfu, the director of the railway, plans to recruit disaster victims to build it, which can accommodate 5,000 disaster laborers, because Zhejiang Province suffered a severe disaster last autumn. He has telegraphed Zhang Zonghai, the county magistrate of Xiaoshan, to come to the province to discuss the method of recruiting labor.

Jiaxing 80

Suicide Due to Economic Pressure

On the night of the 21st, a male traveler arrived at the Weixing Hotel on Weixin Street in the northern city of Jiaxing. He was wearing a cotton robe and had a sad expression. He booked a room and claimed to be 31 years old, named Jiang Zhenting, a native of Songjiang, and a Jinghuo merchant. He went out once and returned to the hotel to sleep. Until the afternoon of the 22nd, he had not gotten up. The hotel staff pried open the door and entered, and saw that his expression was different. They questioned him, and he said he was sick. After being questioned again, he said he had swallowed opium. The hotel sent him to Dexin Hospital for treatment. However, the poison had already entered his internal organs, and although he was rescued, it was ineffective. He died in the evening. Only two small foreign coins and a few copper coins were found on his body, and a suicide note was found in his bedroom. The note said, "To the hotel, please forgive me. Recently, business has declined, and I have been unemployed for several months. Economic difficulties make it impossible to maintain my livelihood, so I commit suicide by taking poison. Please forgive me for everything. Jiang Zhenting from Songjiang, handwritten." Judging from his words, he committed suicide because he was economically pressured and unable to survive. The hotel has reported to the local branch of the court and sent someone to examine the body. After setting up a coffin, they are trying to find the relatives to claim the body.

Xiaoshan 81

Bandits Rob Night Boats

Two passenger boats sailing from Shaoxing to Xiaoshan near Qianqing, Dongxiang, Xiaoshan, encountered two bandit boats blocking their way around dawn on the 22nd at Qianmei. The bandits pretended to check the mail and ordered them to dock along the coast. They boarded the boats and ransacked them, taking all the foreign mail and cloth, totaling more than 300 yuan. Nineteen male and female passengers were searched, and each person lost three to five yuan. Furthermore, the boatman A Wei hid five foreign mails in the bottom of the cabin, but was spotted by a bandit, who stabbed him in the leg with a bayonet, and he fainted on the ground.

Ningbo 82

Youth Commits Suicide Due to Unemployment

Sun Caixing, a native of Jiangcun in southern Yin, is 24 years old. Both of his parents are alive, and he has a younger brother and sister. He is engaged, but not yet married. Caixing worked as a partner in the Yuandong Shoe Store on Dongdu Road in Ningbo. Because the store's business was slow, the employees were laid off, and Caixing was dismissed. Caixing has been unemployed since then. Fearing being ridiculed by his neighbors if he returns to his hometown, he stayed with friends in Ningbo, thinking of finding a place to eat. However, in this time of commercial depression and overstaffing, he has been unable to find a suitable job for a month. His life has been miserable, and he has the idea of suicide. Yesterday afternoon at 4:00, he booked room number 9 at the Mingzhou Hotel on Lingqiao Road and committed suicide by taking medicine. When the waiter discovered it, he had already died. A suicide note to his father, Sun Shunsheng, was found on the table, saying that the current situation is difficult and there is no interest in living, so he committed suicide.

New County Magistrate Takes Office

The provincial government has approved Guo Ping's resignation as the County Magistrate of Hefei and appointed Zhao Xiaosan, the secretary of the Third District Administrative Commissioner's Office stationed in Liu'an, as his successor. Zhao has arrived in Hefei from the province by car and took office on the 17th. Former County Magistrate Guo will leave Hefei within days.

Large-Scale Banditry in the Northeast Township

More than a thousand bandits have gathered in the Nangangji and Wenji areas of the northeast township, creating a formidable force. The people are suffering. The county security first and second teams advanced to suppress the bandits a few days ago and fought with the bandits in Wenji. Due to their weak forces, they requested assistance. Liu Zhige, the deputy of the security headquarters, personally led the third, fourth, and fifth teams to rush to the front last night to assist in the suppression to eliminate the bandits.

Local News

China Labor Association Established Yesterday 84

Tao Baichuan, Li Pingheng, etc., Elected as Directors

According to the Central News Agency, the China Labor Association held its founding meeting at the auditorium of the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions in Meijialong at 1:00 PM yesterday. More than 300 representatives attended the meeting, passed the constitution, elected directors, and issued a declaration. The meeting adjourned at about 4:00 PM. The details are as follows:

Attending Representatives: Those who attended yesterday included Tong Hangbai and Zhang Xiaotong from the Municipal Party Department, members Lu Jingshi, Tao Baichuan, Cheng Haifeng, Zhu Xuefan, Zhou Xuexiang, Zhao Shusheng, Ye Xianggao, Li Mengnan, Shui Xiangyun, Zhang Risheng, Dai Youheng, Lu Yunshu, Yu Yaoqiu, Liu Xinquan, all the students of the Workers' Training Department, the postal workers' Boy Scouts, and guests Zhu Shuren, etc., more than 300 people.

Chairman's Report: Chairman Lu Jingshi delivered the opening speech, saying, "Everyone, today is the day when the China Labor Association holds its founding meeting. The association has been initiated and prepared for three months. In these three months, we have legally completed the procedures and obtained the approval of the party and government agencies. Today, we are honored to have the party and government representatives give instructions and the guests enthusiastically participate, which shows great gratitude. The purpose of our establishment of this association is that the labor circles across the country believe that in the current environment, the production movement is needed, and it is necessary to engage in labor. If this is the case, the entire country will be able to be saved, and the labor circles themselves will have a way out. Therefore, the labor circles across the country believe that there must be such an organized organization. In the Soviet Union and Germany, they try their best to improve the ability of service and labor. Only those who can labor and serve loyally can have a happy life. This spirit is full of vigor. Today, the atmosphere of decay is permeated throughout the country. It is necessary to inject this vigor to arouse the people across the country to work hard. We are all engaged in the labor circles. In the future, we will formulate a work program and gradually realize it. This is the purpose and meaning of this association. This association will not only seek the welfare of the labor circles across the country and make the people across the country attach importance to the labor cause, but also seek to contact the world labor movement."

Preparation Process: After the chairman's report, Zhu Xuefan, a member of the preparatory committee, reported on the preparation process, saying, "The gentlemen who are enthusiastic about the labor movement and the labor circles first initiated the organization of the China Labor Association. However, because we feel that the mission of this association is great and the meaning is important, it is not something that a few people can shoulder. We have to seek it widely. In addition to continuing to recruit members in this city, we also seek membership from the gentlemen engaged in labor across the country. At the same time, we are legally handling the filing procedures with the party and government agencies. In the preparatory work, these two things are the most important. Now, in addition to Shanghai, there are also Beijing, Nanjing, Hankou, Luoyang, and other places participating in this association. After the establishment of this association, we not only hope that the labor circles across the country can practically seek the progress of the labor cause, but also hope that other circles can also give assistance from time to time, so that the association's affairs can be improved day by day."

Representatives' Instructions: Tong Hangbai, a representative of the Municipal Party Department, gave instructions, saying, "The establishment of the China Labor Association today is more important than the establishment of a certain trade union, because the Labor Association seeks the welfare of the entire labor circles, while a certain trade union is only limited to a certain part of the labor circles. The importance of the position of the labor circles in the entire nation is known to everyone. Moreover, since the serious national disasters suffered by our country since the 'September 18th' and 'January 28th' incidents have made the fate of the country in a state of extreme anxiety. Today, the people of the country all know that the country's fate is in danger, and they have come out to create the proposition of saving the country, but there are many propositions of saving the country, and I am afraid that it cannot be effective. Today, for the way of saving the country, there is nothing better than gathering the national power. In other words, it is to unite the strength of the entire nation and use it for the country. The labor circles are one of the most powerful parts of the entire nation. In the past, the labor circles were also affected by the atmosphere of decline. Today, we deeply hope that after the establishment of this association, it can be like a fierce bomb, thrown into the silent air, and in a bang, it can shake its silent air and turn it into an active air. Moreover, the importance of the position of the labor circles in the entire nation means that in the future, we not only hope that the labor circles themselves can be practically combined and show their great strength, but also promote other circles to get excited together and seek the liberation of the entire nation. On behalf of the Municipal Party Department, I hope that your association can fully exert its spirit and gradually complete the established plan." Subsequently, Cui Conghao, a representative of the Social Affairs Bureau, delivered a speech, saying, "I express my congratulations to the labor circles across the country for the establishment of your association. However, I still have a hope for your association. The responsible persons of your association should strictly prevent the moths of the labor circles from mixing in and practically protect the interests of the labor circles, and make the labor affairs proceed smoothly." Cheng Haifeng, the director of the China Branch of the International Labor Bureau, delivered a speech, saying, "On behalf of the International Labor Bureau, I express my great joy for the establishment of your association, and I am very happy for the future of the world labor movement. I am willing to cooperate sincerely in all future work of your association. I also see that the purpose of your association is perfect, and all those who participate in this association are practically engaged in the labor movement and are experienced, so I deeply congratulate the Chinese labor movement on its bright future."

Election of Directors: After the speeches, the constitution was passed and the election began. As a result of the election, the formal directors Tao Baichuan, Li Pingheng, Cheng Haifeng, Wu Huan, Lu Jingshi, Zhu Xuefan, Zhu Maocheng, Zhao Shusheng, Wu Shaoshu, Yu Jiayong, Zhou Jiaxiang, Fu Dewei, Wang Yongsheng, Zhang Xiaotong, Zhang Jianbai, Shui Xiangyun, Chen Wenbin, Wen Zhuangyou, Zhang Daomin, etc., were elected. The alternate directors elected were Lu Yinshu, Han Dayong, Zhou Bingwen, Wang Yisheng, Guo Tian, Wang Jiashu, Li Mengnan, Ye Xianggao, Zhang Guangdai, etc.

Declaration of the General Assembly: China's labor movement has made rapid progress in recent years with the progress of the National Revolution. Not only are the second organization labor training, labor legislation, and labor welfare undertakings now roughly in scale, but also the general public's views and attitudes toward laborers and the labor movement have become more correct than before. I remember when Chairman Chiang Kai-shek began to advocate the New Life Movement, he put forward the slogan "Labor is the source of happiness" and established the method of "National Labor Service." Recently, in the letter to compatriots on the first anniversary of the New Movement, he further advocated "Life is productionized" and praised the greatness of labor. This is the gospel of the Chinese labor movement. These are the gains of the labor movement in recent years. However, if we look at the bright side, it is so. If we look at the dark side, there are indeed many shortcomings. First, although workers have organizations, the organizations are not all sound. Labor training is also not very successful. Second, although important labor laws and regulations are generally available, some parts are just lip service and do not reach the reality. Third, because of the rapid economic aggression of imperialism, the development of China's national industry has been affected, and the welfare undertakings of workers cannot be generally established. Fourth, although there are many urban workers with trade union organizations, there are no joint organizations between trade unions in one place and trade unions in other places, resulting in a lack of central strength, and scholars who study labor issues and social figures who sympathize with the labor movement, laborers, and labor groups do not realize that there is an organized connection, which somewhat affects the progress of the labor movement. Fifth, the labor movement has been advocated for more than ten years, but in addition to the general principles of the Three People's Principles, we do not have a detailed work program for the labor movement. These are all undeniable shortcomings in the labor movement. In order to remedy the defects and adapt to the needs of the facts, the China Labor Association was organized and established on February 24th, 24th year of the Republic of China. Based on the purpose of the establishment of this association, we have formulated a work program to be the goal of our future efforts. The full text is recorded below:

Work Program: "Work Program of China Labor Association" This association is organized by various individuals or groups in the labor circles, as well as those who study labor issues or are engaged in the labor movement, to create labor theory and implement labor control. The work program is formulated as follows: (1) General Outline: Confirm the Three People's Principles as the highest principle of the Chinese labor movement. On the one hand, passively eliminate the ideology of class struggle, and on the other hand, actively promote the spirit of labor-management coordination, in order to strive for the construction of production undertakings and labor welfare, and seek the implementation of our party's labor policy. (2) In terms of education, advocate the dualism of "labor education" and "education labor", refer to the modern educational trend, and vigorously promote the universality of labor education, and promote national sports as much as possible, implement military training, and enhance the physical strength of self-defense. (3) In terms of production, we must rely on national interests, contribute ability and sacrifice freedom as a fashion, and take hard work and frugality as a creed. We must eliminate the bad habits of stealing, being passive, jealous, decadent, selfish, and opportunistic, and actively increase the nation's productivity. (4) In terms of welfare, we will work together to promote the undertaking of cooperation, labor insurance, labor nurseries, etc., in order to enrich the economic self-sufficiency of laborers. (5) In terms of organization, advocate taking courtesy, justice, integrity, and shame as the center, and diligence, thrift, neatness, cleanliness as the basis, and develop new life habits of being responsible, disciplined, believing in leaders, and obeying groups. (6) In terms of culture, advocate taking the Three People's Principles as the center, indicate the fallacy of communism and capitalism, eliminate cruel and hypocritical proletarian propaganda, and create a positive, scientific, and national labor culture. (7) In terms of relief, we will organize unemployment registration, job placement, and vocational guidance to relieve the panic of unemployment, and establish labor hospitals to solve the suffering of laborers. (8) In terms of legislation, we will adopt the modern legislative spirit of various countries, study the advantages and disadvantages of domestic labor codes, and suggest that the government improve labor legislation. The above is all the experience of our colleagues in researching and engaging in the labor movement in recent years. At the beginning of the establishment of this association, we would like to inform the people of the country and hope that we can encourage each other. China Labor Association, February 23rd.

Various Groups Meet to Discuss Relief, Market Recovery is Expected 86

Three Banks Prepare to Launch Goods Mortgage Loans

Money and Banking Industries Release Loans as Much as Possible to Stabilize the Market

Since the Shanghai market has been depressed, after the local association, the municipal chamber of commerce, the money and banking industry association, and other national organizations held meetings for days to discuss the relief plan, and after the Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi expressed his best efforts to maintain it, the market has gradually stabilized and recovery is promising. A reporter from Xinxin News Agency learned from various parties yesterday that (1) the Central, China, and Transportation Banks have started preparing to launch goods mortgage loans. Once the amount of loans and detailed methods are determined, they can be implemented. The method will be modeled after the previous money and banking industry mortgage loans. However, the goods will be converted at the market price, and the daily dismantling market will be announced by the Central Bank every day. (2) The money and banking industries had previously resolved to tighten loans and restrict real estate mortgages, which had a great impact on the market. Real estate is one of the largest enterprises in Shanghai, and its prosperity and decline are closely related to the market. In view of this, the money and banking industries have expressed that in order to revive the market, they will appropriately increase the amount of real estate mortgages and handle the acceptance of various goods as usual. (3) Since the Ministry of Finance implemented the method of rewarding the import of foreign silver, major Chinese and foreign banks will have a large amount of cash transferred to Shanghai to regulate. At the same time, the Ping City Committee has purchased a large amount of cash from London, which will arrive in Shanghai in mid-next month. In the future, Shanghai's capital is expected to increase day by day, so the Shanghai market has gradually stabilized and recovery is promising.

The plan must be resolved and announced by the Financial Advisory Committee

According to the Guowen News Agency, major banks in the city, due to the recent economic downturn and reluctance from outside parties to accept warehouse receipt mortgages, convened a meeting at 4 PM yesterday at the Shanghai Bankers' Association Joint Preparatory Committee at 59 Hong Kong Road. Estonia's National Day Celebrated Yesterday 88

Estonian Residents Hold Celebration Ceremony

Yesterday marked the 27th anniversary of the declaration of independence of the Republic of Estonia. Although the number of Estonian residents in this port is not large, they are very united. They gathered at the Estonian Consulate last night to hold a celebration, chaired by Honorary Consul Lundborg, who has held this position since 1922. Estonia was ruled in turn by Germany, Denmark, and Sweden for seven hundred years, and for the last two hundred years, it was incorporated into Russian territory. Because of its position as a cultural and commercial intermediary between East and West, major powers often wanted to seize it for themselves. After losing their freedom, the Estonian people never forgot their ambition to restore their country. The outbreak of the European War provided an opportunity, and with the help of the British Navy and Finnish volunteers, they launched a righteous uprising against Russia and finally achieved their goal.

All Sectors Value the Increased Issuance of Banknotes by Foreign Banks 93

Hoping the Government Finds a Way to Stop It

So as Not to Affect China's Finances

According to the Xinsheng News Agency, the case of foreign banks increasing the issuance of convertible notes is highly valued by all parties. If it is realized, it will have a significant impact on China's finances. The details learned by the reporter of the Xinsheng News Agency are recorded below.

Various Sectors Value the Increased Issuance of Banknotes　The earliest established foreign bank is the British-owned Mercantile Bank, which was established in 1853. The next is the British-owned HSBC, which was established in 1864, before any banks in China. It has a history of several decades and has issued banknotes in China. In recent years, it has gradually decreased. Recently, it has been rumored that HSBC and other banks will increase the issuance of banknotes, which has been valued by all parties, and it is hoped that the government authorities will find a way to stop it, so as not to affect China's finances.

Total Amount of Banknotes Issued by Foreign Banks　As of December 31, 1932, the total amount of convertible notes issued by various foreign banks was as follows: Mercantile Bank £1,894,552; HSBC HK$137,449,255; Chartered Bank £162,110; Deutsch-Asiatische Bank Taels 41,811; Yokohama Specie Bank ¥6,598,139; Bank of Taiwan ¥52,666,450; Bank of Chosen ¥125,210,153; Citibank US$2,000,000; Banque Franco-Chinoise $237,290 Chinese currency; Banque de l'Indochine Francs 965,045,740; Banque Belge pour l'Etranger (issued in China) Francs 3,775,220. Since 1933, the amount of convertible notes issued by foreign banks in China has gradually decreased. Those commonly circulating in the market are HSBC, Mercantile Bank, Chartered Bank, Banque Franco-Chinoise, Banque Belge pour l'Etranger, Citibank, and other banks.

Ministry of Finance Approves Chamber of Commerce's Explanation That Purchase Manuals Are Exempt from Stamp Duty 101

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the China Chemical Industry Society requesting an explanation as to whether the employee purchase discount manual should be stamped. The Chamber telegraphed the Ministry of Finance for clarification last month. The Chamber received a reply from the Ministry of Finance yesterday. The original text is recorded below: The telegram and sample manual have been received. Since the employees of the China Chemical Industry Society purchase goods by paying cash according to the preferential price and are given a shipping invoice with payment and delivery at any time, the preferential manual issued is only for restricting the quantity of purchases and is not used to withdraw goods. It is different in nature from the manual for withdrawing money and goods as stipulated in the Provisional Regulations on Stamp Duty. It should be temporarily exempted from stamping. You should immediately inform and notify. This is the reply.

Land Value Tax in South Shanghai and Other Districts Scheduled to Begin Collection 102

March 1st

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Finance has determined that the first phase of the land value tax for 1935 in Districts 1 to 7 of the South Shanghai District, Districts 1 to 4 of the Fahua District, and Districts 5, 6, and 8 of the Yinxiang District will begin on March 1st of this year. From the date of collection, there is a deadline of two months for completion, ending on April 30th of this year. Those who fail to complete the payment after the deadline will be summoned and pursued in accordance with Article 8 of the Provisional Regulations on the Collection of Land Value Tax and Article 23 of the Implementing Rules, and annual interest will be levied on the amount owed, and the income of the land will be extracted and auctioned for compensation according to the number of years of arrears, in order to comply with the regulations and emphasize tax collection.

Chamber of Commerce Telegraphed the Ministry of Railways Again to Request Repayment of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Purchase Bond 103

Purchase Bonds Cannot Be Compared to Old Debts of Distant Years

The Business and Transportation Conference Resolved to Repay Them First

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Railways yesterday, saying, "To the Ministry of Railways in Nanjing, on the 22nd of this month, we received a letter from the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Purchase Bond Holders Association stating that on the 12th of this month, we received your letter of the 11th, indicating that you had forwarded a telegram to the Ministry of Railways, ordering the Railway Bureau to take into account the agreement and not to extend it again. It also stated that you had received the Ministry of Railways' Geng telegram, which stated, "We have received the telegram, and regarding the case of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Purchase Bond holders requesting the return of principal and interest, the Ministry has repeatedly received petitions from the bondholders, which have been forwarded to the Railway for review and response. We have also telegraphed the Railway to promptly discuss and determine a plan and announce it to the bondholders for negotiation." We have listened to all of this and are very grateful. We have now received the Ministry of Railways' approval No. 49 on February 7, which stated, "We have received the report of January 22 of this year. The Tianjin-Pukou Railway has many debts, and the reorganization plan must be planned as a whole. The repeated postponement of the repayment of the principal of the purchase bond is based on the economic situation of the Railway. The various points mentioned in the report are mostly ignorant of the facts. In addition to ordering a prompt overall review and response for approval, this is the approval for notification." We were deeply surprised after receiving this. The Tianjin-Pukou Railway Bureau issued 1 million yuan of purchase bonds in 1928, and the regulations stated on the face of the bond that the locomotives and rolling stock purchased with this bond and the Railway's surplus profits would be used as collateral, and it was determined that from January 1931, the principal and interest would be paid off in ten months, except for April and September. According to what is stated on the face of the bond, there was originally no room for extension. However, the Railway Bureau first extended the period by two years due to the impact of the war on revenue. On February 4, 1933, the Railway clearly replied that the purchase bond tickets should be drawn for repayment of principal and supplementary payment of interest, and a plan had been drafted and submitted to the Ministry for instructions. Once approved, it would be announced, but there was no news of implementation afterwards. Until December 20 of the same year, the Railway issued a notice again, stating that it would be extended again for one year from 1934 for repayment. In summary, the Railway has treated its own credit as nothing, repeatedly breaking its promises, not understanding the suffering of merchants. The period of this extension has passed again, and there is still no clear repayment plan. After our detailed statement requesting immediate repayment, the Ministry did not plan for immediate repayment and accused us of being ignorant of the facts, and used the name of overall planning to delay the repayment period. It is not known that this bond has a specified guarantee and a limited repayment date, which is a specially ordered debt. How can it be mixed with other debts? It is very clear that it should not be planned as a whole. Moreover, the debt has been resolved by the National Business and Transportation Conference convened by the Ministry of Railways to give priority to repayment, and it goes without saying that it cannot be compared with other debts. We still ask for your righteousness to urge the Ministry of Railways to instruct the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Bureau to repay the debt on a specific date. The purchase bond is a new debt that has arisen in recent years. The amount is not huge, the agreed repayment period is short, and the locomotives and rolling stock purchased with the bond are used as collateral. It cannot be compared with old debts of distant years. The National Business and Transportation Conference also has a resolution to give priority to repayment. It seems that the old debt reorganization plan should not be applied, which would violate credit. According to the previous letter, we hereby telegram again to the Ministry for review and approval, and it is in the public interest to handle it as requested by the bondholders association. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce bows."

Ministry of Communications Approves China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to Borrow Money to Purchase Ships 106

But Five Points Must Be Noted

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's board of directors submitted a plan to the Ministry of Communications to borrow money from the Shanghai banking community to purchase ships to transport goods for the Longhai Intermodal Transport, and the Ministry of Communications instructed its approval. The original order said, "All submitted documents have been received. Purchase should be approved, and the funds can be borrowed from the Shanghai banking community by the Bureau. However, before the purchase, the following should be noted: (1) The ship's draft is 21 feet 9 inches. If it is fully loaded, it may not be able to enter the Haizhou Port, because the water in Lianyungang is only 18 feet when it is shallow. According to the report, the ship is used to transport wood and cotton, so the calculation is about 3,000 tons of cargo each time, and the draft can be reduced. However, it should be verified that if the ship carries about 3,000 tons of cargo and cannot freely enter and exit Lianyungang, the purchase should be stopped. (2) The appearance, hull condition, and internal equipment of the ship have not been stated. A simple drawing should be provided to clarify the situation and facilitate inspection. (3) Whether the boiler and smoke pipe or water pipe and other important components of the ship are in good condition should be checked before purchase. (4) The speed of the ship, according to the report, is 9 nautical miles per hour. It should be clarified whether it is the maximum speed or the ordinary speed. (5) The business estimate of the ship does not include depreciation, which should be added to the calculation of profit and loss. The above points should be followed."

Shenxin No. 5 Factory Declares Shutdown 107

More Than 2,000 Employees Lose Their Jobs

According to the Huadong News Agency, the Shenxin No. 5 Textile Factory (formerly Deda) at 1316 Huade Road was founded in 1914, with the Rongs as managers, Rong Weiren as the factory director, and Zeng Xiangxi as the chief engineer. The registered capital was 1.3 million taels, with 54,208 spindles and 12,720 thread spindles, and more than 2,131 employees.

Reasons for Shutdown　In recent years, the price of yarn has been cheap and the price of cotton has been expensive to the extreme. Under the leadership of the Rongs, the factory was fortunate not to fail. By the time of the Spring Festival, after the final settlement, the decline of the yarn industry reached its peak. Although the Rongs tried their best to plan, there was no solution, resulting in the official declaration of temporary shutdown on the 16th of this month.

Aftermath Problems　Since the factory shut down, more than 2,000 workers have suddenly lost their support, resulting in the organization of a petition delegation to request relief from relevant Party and government departments. The workers deeply understand the Rongs' difficulties and are actually acting out of desperation. It is said that some workers are willing to reduce their wages, but due to factual difficulties, it has not been possible to fulfill their wishes so far. As for Rong himself, he is actively planning to start the factory again. According to relevant departments, the banking syndicate related to Shenxin should urgently seek a relief plan for this incident in order to maintain it, to maintain the livelihood of more than 2,000 people, and to support this basic national industry.

The Inland Navigation Association Strives for Cooperation Rights on Inland Waterways 108

Revised to Include Cooperative Clauses

Urging Fellow Businesses to Pay Attention

The Dagong She reports that when the Ministry of Transportation held a meeting last year to promote the shipping industry, it instructed the former Shanghai Shipping Association to collaborate with the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to establish a Shipping Cooperation Design Committee. A plan was drafted and preparations were underway. However, the Inland River Steamboat Association of this city, feeling that the plan excluded inland river businesses and was of great significance to the inland navigation industry itself, submitted a reasoned argument to fellow businesses. The original text stated: Since the Ministry of Transportation convened a national shipping conference in Beijing in March of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934) to promote the shipping industry, the most important resolution was to promote effective cooperation in the national shipping industry. It was agreed upon to implement two methods, A and B. Method B stipulated that the Shanghai Shipping Association, following the Ministry's approval of the resolution, would join with the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to form the China Shipping Cooperation Design Committee to plan specific cooperation schemes. On August 23rd, Mr. Chen Bogang, the Secretary-General of the former Shipping Association, sent a letter to the Chairman Zhang of this Association, suggesting that the issue of shipping cooperation had been privately decided by both parties. Inland river businesses should participate in the cooperation based on the principle of line division. On September 7th, this Association submitted a document to the China Shipping Cooperation Design Committee, clearly stating that inland river navigation should be based on the principle of line division and incorporated into the specific cooperation scheme. On September 13th, this Association received a letter from the committee stating that, after a supplementary discussion at the temporary committee on the 11th of this month, a special clause had been drafted and included in the scheme. However, the specific cooperation scheme for Chinese shipping, approved by the Ministry of Transportation on December 29th of the 23rd year of the Republic, instruction number 22149, only included clauses for harbor vessels and did not have a special clause for inland river vessels. This Association considered the matter of inland river cooperation to be of great importance and raised it for discussion at the 50th Executive Committee meeting. It was resolved to: (1) request the preparatory office of the China Shipping Cooperative to copy the original text and plan submitted to the Ministry of Transportation by the former Design Committee for reference; (2) formulate the principle of line division for inland river businesses and hold a joint meeting with inland river business associations to promote progress; (3) convene a temporary general meeting of members to jointly discuss cooperation methods. On February 3rd, this Association received a letter from the preparatory office of the China Shipping Cooperative stating that after the China Shipping Cooperation Design Committee approved this Association's request to include inland river lines in the scheme, it was passed at a meeting and a separate clause was drafted, added as Article 24 of the scheme, which stated: "Small boats operating on various inland river lines shall cooperate according to line, and profits and losses shall be calculated separately." It also added an explanation, submitted to the Ministry for inspection and approval. Later, an instruction and the scheme were received, indicating that there were still unsatisfactory points that needed correction, and specifically pointed out that Article 24 should be deleted and revised. After the meeting, the Ministry's instructions were followed for separate revisions and submitted for approval. Therefore, the scheme did not include clauses for inland river lines because it was handled according to the Ministry's instructions. This Association believes that the above-mentioned sections clearly show that the Ministry and the Cooperation Design Committee are depriving us of the right to cooperate on inland river lines. This Association considers this matter to be of great importance to the future safety and security of the inland river shipping industry, and should proceed with implementation in accordance with the resolutions of the 50th meeting. We hope that our fellow businesses will argue on reasonable grounds.

Jiang Kanghu's Second Lecture on the Ten Admonitions for a Good Life 111

Yesterday afternoon at four o'clock, Dr. Jiang Kanghu gave the second lecture on the Ten Admonitions for a Good Life at the YMCA in the Eight Immortals Bridge. The lecture covered the third admonition, "Sleeping in the Open," and the fourth admonition, "Waking Up Early." Dr. Jiang specifically hired the Bingxun Shorthand Society of Kade Road Shanchang Lane to record the lecture. More than 500 people attended. The main points of the lecture are recorded below. Dr. Jiang said that Zeng Guofan often used the four characters "renting books, pigs, vegetables" to encourage his descendants. I also have the four characters "cloth, vegetables, dew, walking" to encourage myself. I have already discussed "wearing cloth" and "eating vegetables." "Dew" is "sleeping in the open," and "walking" is "walking." I absolutely practice the first two, and I relatively practice the latter two. I sleep in the open in warm and sunny weather in spring and autumn, and I walk when time and energy permit. "Sleeping in the open" does not mean without shelter, but rather fully obtaining sunlight and air. Westerners sleep with their windows wide open, which is very beneficial to health. The Chinese do the opposite, which should be improved. Next, he talked about getting up early. Dr. Jiang advocated sleeping for six hours. The concern is not lack of sleep, but rather sleeping without truly sleeping. Insomnia not only affects the body but also affects one's career. The best way to remedy insomnia is through intense work and more exercise. In this way, a tired body will surely get a sound sleep, and getting up early is especially necessary.

Highway Association Holds Highway Essay Competition 112

In order to solicit opinions from all walks of life on highway issues, the China National Highway Construction Association held a meeting of the standing directors yesterday and decided to hold a highway issue essay competition to gather opinions for reference in highway construction. The brief rules are recorded below: (1) The essay is divided into two topics: one is "How to build the most economical and practical highway," and the other is "Can developing highways help rural areas?" Contributors may choose one topic. (2) The essay must be written entirely in the national language, and clarity and fluency are required (classical or vernacular language is acceptable). Each essay should be limited to 10,000 words. Whether or not the manuscript is accepted, the original will not be returned. (3) The essay must be written on square grid paper. If there are photos, charts, etc., please attach them separately. (4) All essays must be sent to the Association at 70 Gubai Road, Shanghai, before June 20th of the 24th year of the Republic (1935). (5) The submitted essays will be evaluated separately by experts hired by the Association. The titles of the evaluators are listed on the left (in order of the number of strokes in their surnames): Shen Yi, Gao Enhong, Ye Gongchuo, Dong Xiujia, Zhao Zukang, Li Zhaohuan, Fan Guang. (6) After the essays are selected, they will be announced in newspapers in a news format in mid-August. The selected essays will be published in the Association's Highway Monthly. (7) The number of winners is limited to ten. The award method is as follows: the first prize is 100 yuan, the second prize is 50 yuan, the third prize is 20 yuan, and the fourth to tenth prizes are a complete set of books published by the Association and a one-year subscription to Highway Monthly. The names and photos of all winners will be published in Highway Monthly and kept by the Association for commemoration.

A Patrolman's Wife and a Rickshaw Puller Commit Adultery 117

Sentenced to Three Months of Imprisonment Each

Peng Shaoxiang, from Yancheng, Jiangbei, is 23 years old. He married Wang (approximately the same age as Peng), a woman from the same village, as his wife. They have been married for six years and have one son and one daughter each. Peng and his wife originally farmed in their hometown for a living. Recently, due to the bankruptcy of the rural areas in their hometown, they came to Shanghai together last year to make a living. They lived together in the back building of No. 6 Wufeng Lane, Kangdi Road, in the French Concession. After Peng arrived in Shanghai, he first made a living as a peddler, and then pulled a rickshaw. Recently, he was recruited as a patrolman in the French Concession Police Department. As a result, the family's life was slightly better than before, and they lived happily together. Jiang Deshe, also from the same village and an acquaintance of Peng, is 35 years old. He used to pull a rickshaw for a certain family for a living. He lived alone in the attic below Peng's house. He often joked with Peng's wife, Wang. Recently, he developed an affair with Wang. At about 5 AM on the 21st of this month, Jiang took advantage of Peng's absence from duty and sneaked into the room to carry out the cuckoo's nest plan, engaging in a secret rendezvous with Wang. They were in the midst of passion when Peng happened to forget his clothes and returned home to retrieve them. He suddenly saw his wife and Jiang naked, sleeping in the same bed. Peng was consumed by jealousy and immediately grabbed Jiang and reprimanded him. Jiang, in desperation, knelt on the ground and begged Peng to forgive him. At that moment, Peng was in a hurry to go to the police station for duty, so he did not pursue the matter and released Jiang. At about 10 AM that day, Peng returned home from his shift and saw Jiang still sitting on the bed with his wife, talking and laughing. Therefore, unable to vent his anger, he reported to the police station and sent Detective Jiang Shaotang to bring Jiang and Wang to the police station. The day before yesterday, they were sent to the Criminal Division 8 of the Special Court No. 2. Fee Xizhen, the lawyer of the police station, stated the case and prosecuted them for the crime of disrupting the family according to Article 256 of the Criminal Code, requesting legal action. Then, the plaintiff described the previous situation. When Wang was interrogated, she confessed that when her husband went out for duty yesterday morning, she was sleeping in bed. Jiang Deshe suddenly broke into the room and raped her. At the time, she refused, but he claimed that her husband owed him 9 yuan and 40 cents, which had not been repaid. If she allowed him to have sexual intercourse, the debt would be waived. Therefore, she was temporarily deceived and defiled. Jiang Deshe confessed that he had been in a relationship with Wang since June of last year and had had intercourse three times. The rest of his words were evasive. After verification by Judge Qiu Huanying, the court sentenced Peng's wife, Wang, to continuous adultery, and Jiang Deshe to continuous adultery with a married woman, each sentenced to three months of imprisonment as a warning.

Major Fire at Gonghexiang Warehouse 119

Burning from Midnight Until 10:30 AM Before Being Extinguished

Valuable Goods All Reduced to Ashes, Fortunately No Injuries

——Losses of Goods Exceed 500,000 Yuan——

Yesterday morning, a major fire occurred at Warehouse No. 26 of Gonghexiang Wharf on Huade Road. Valuable goods stored in the warehouse and goods deposited by the customs were all reduced to ashes. The losses were extremely heavy, exceeding 500,000 yuan. The fire started at around 3 AM yesterday morning. It was discovered by the warehouse keeper at 5:10 AM, by which time it had already broken through the roof. By the time the fire brigade arrived, the interior had been completely destroyed. It was not extinguished until 10:30 AM, truly a catastrophic event.

Warehouse Contents. The Gonghexiang Wharf on Huade Road is owned by Gonghexiang Wharf Co., Ltd. The land is very vast, with a total area of ​​several thousand meters. The land is represented by Jardine Matheson & Co., Ltd. and is insured against fire with Jardine Matheson. Entering the wharf through the main gate, Warehouse No. 26 is a magnificent building with three floors. On the 22nd of this month, the Norwegian ship Tokyo arrived in Shanghai and docked at the wharf. Workers were hired to unload the cargo. From the day before yesterday to yesterday, more than 2,000 pieces of coconut oil, more than 3,000 pieces of iron wire, and more than 1,500 pieces of sundries, foreign goods, and medicines were unloaded and stored on the ground floor of the warehouse. At that time, the second floor of the warehouse was filled with sundries, and the third floor was a customs warehouse, filled with miscellaneous foreign goods such as artificial silk, felt hats, and leather shoes deposited by the customs. These goods were all goods that had not paid customs duties and were deposited here by the customs. They could only be taken out after paying the taxes.

Fire Situation. The Norwegian ship had not finished unloading the day before yesterday and stopped that night, planning to resume unloading yesterday morning. However, at 5:10 AM yesterday morning, just as dawn was breaking, the warehouse keeper suddenly saw heavy smoke rising from the roof. He rushed to investigate and realized that the warehouse was on fire. He immediately sounded the alarm and called for help. At the same time, he reported to the police station by telephone. The Shanghai Municipal Council Police Department, together with the nearby fire brigade, drove more than ten fire trucks to put out the fire. Unfortunately, most of the warehouse had already been destroyed by the fire. Because artificial silk, coconut oil, and other materials were extremely flammable, the fire continued to rage despite the firefighters' efforts. It was not until 10:30 AM yesterday morning that all the goods in the warehouse were burned, and the fire was extinguished. Warehouse No. 26 was reduced to an empty shell, with scorched tiles and ashes as far as the eye could see. The tragic scene was unbearable.

Cause of the Accident. According to investigations, the cause of the accident was that some of the coconut oil unloaded from the Norwegian ship on the ground floor was extremely flammable. At around 3 or 4 AM the night before last (yesterday morning), a burning object combined with the coconut oil on the ground floor (one theory is that it was unextinguished cigarette butts). The fire then spread, and in an instant, a small spark ignited a large area, and smoke and fire filled the air, rushing from the ground floor directly to the second and third floors and breaking through the roof. At that time, because coconut oil and artificial silk and other goods seized by the customs on the third floor were extremely flammable, the fire became uncontrollable once it started. There were five people guarding the warehouse, and they only became aware of the fire after it broke through the roof at 5:10 AM yesterday morning. Because the fire started in the northern part of the ground floor, no one was inside at first, and they were unaware of the fire. At 5:10 AM, the Central Fire Brigade dispatched a large number of fire trucks, more than ten in total, to rescue and extinguish the fire by spraying water from fire hoses. Unfortunately, the coconut oil on the ground floor was extremely flammable, and adding water on top of oil made it even more difficult to extinguish. On the contrary, it was not until 10:30 AM that the entire warehouse had been burned down and the fire was extinguished.

Police Investigation. The General Patrol Police Department dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives, together with the fire brigade, to assist in the rescue and protection after the accident. An investigation was conducted into the losses suffered. Because no estimate had been made, the exact number was not yet available. However, all the goods stored in the warehouse were extremely valuable, and the quantity was very large. The losses were estimated to be more than 500,000 yuan. According to a spokesperson for Gonghexiang Wharf Co., Ltd., the construction of the warehouse and the goods inside were all insured by Jardine Matheson, so there should be no losses. The goods unloaded by the Norwegian ship were also insured and unaffected. However, the goods seized by the customs and stored on the third floor of the warehouse were feared to be uninsured. There were also hundreds of coffins deposited in the warehouse by other parties, which were also burned. Fortunately, the fire occurred late at night, and no one was on duty in the warehouse, so no one was killed, which was a great blessing in misfortune.

Construction of the Qiujiang Wharf 121

The Municipal Government and the Central Bank

Agree on Four Mutually Beneficial Measures

The Central Bank has long been planning and proceeding with the construction of the Qiujiang Wharf. In order to promote the early completion of the wharf, the Municipal Government invited representatives from the Central Bank, Secretary Ling, to exchange opinions and agreed on four mutually beneficial measures: (1) The Central Bank will pay for the construction of roads in the wharf area. (2) The Central Bank will build a public wharf with a shoreline of 50 meters in accordance with the city's plan. (3) The Central Bank must first seek the consent of the Municipal Government for the entire plan of the wharf warehouse and the steps for phased implementation. (4) If the Central Bank transfers the assets of the wharf warehouse, it must first obtain the consent of the Municipal Authority, and the city retains the right to repurchase at a preferential price. It is reported that the above-mentioned measures have been agreed upon by both parties.

The First Special Court Sends Personnel to Hong Kong to Escort Yang Jianping 124

The Detective Who Went to Hong Kong to Escort Hua Zhongchu Will Be Sent Again

Yang Jianping, the former Director-General of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, was impeached by the Supervisory Yuan and reported by the court for corruption and embezzlement of public funds during his tenure. Not only did Yang not surrender and confess his crimes, but he fled to Fujian in the winter of the previous year to participate in the treasonous activities advocated by Chen Mingshu. When the Central Government pacified the Fujian Rebellion, Yang fled to Hong Kong to seek refuge with foreigners. Recently, after negotiations between the Central Government and the Hong Kong authorities for extradition, Yang was detained by Hong Kong officials. Now that he has been captured, he should be extradited and brought to justice according to law to deter corruption. The round trip will take about a week. If the Hong Kong authorities do not object to the extradition, Yang will be able to be brought back to Shanghai by the end of this month.

A Scene of Teacher-Student Romance 125

Marriage Not Yet Approved by Family

Teachers Should Not Be Intimate with Female Students

——Sentenced to One Year, Suspended for Three Years——

Wang Xiaohuai, a native of Shaoxing, 23 years old, resided in the Xiaobanqiao area within the city of his hometown. His father ran a school with many male and female students. Among them was Zhu Muying, a neighbor girl, 16 years old, with beautiful features, who had been studying at the school for eight years. Last spring, Wang's father passed away, and Wang took over as a teacher. Seeing Zhu's beauty and intelligence, and knowing she was not yet betrothed, while Wang himself lacked a suitable spouse, he developed desires. He frequently made flirtatious advances, and they fell in love. In July, they had physical relations. Zhu's mother, Zhu Zhou, was unaware of this. Later, someone acted as a matchmaker, but she refused due to the age difference between Wang and her daughter, and his less affluent family situation. However, the daughter was deeply attached to Wang, vowing to stay with him until old age, but was unable to disobey her mother's wishes, finding herself in a dilemma. Wang had recently been hired as a teacher at a primary school in Jiaxing and entrusted the school to others before going to He to take up the position, hoping to escape the local area and avoid the mother's nagging, planning to discuss things further. Zhu secretly left home on the 17th of this month, went to Jiaxing, found Wang, and asked him to take leave at night. Together, they came to Shanghai and stayed at the residence of a friend surnamed Zhang at No. 3, Yuan Yi Fang, Yangshupu Road. They each sent a letter to Zhu Zhou in Shaoxing, asking to resolve the marriage issue quickly. After her daughter went missing, Zhu Zhou immediately sent people to inquire, learning that she had gone to Jiaxing to find Wang, and then went to Shanghai. She arrived the day before yesterday, learned the location of their residence, and reported it to the Yangshupu police station. The head detective dispatched Liu Changgen to secretly go to the address and arrest Wang, along with Zhu Muying, taking them to the police station for detention. The woman was sent to the Sacred Heart Hospital, where doctors confirmed that her hymen had been ruptured for some time. The next morning, Wang was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court. The Shanghai Municipal Council lawyer, Li Zhishan, detailed the situation and filed a public prosecution for the crime of obstructing marriage under Article 257, Paragraph 1. Subsequently, Zhu Zhou claimed that the defendant should not have induced her daughter to elope. Muying stated that she was not abducted by the defendant but voluntarily wanted to marry him. When questioned, the defendant, with tears streaming down his face, claimed that he did not ask Zhu to come to Jiaxing, and she came to Shanghai to play. He said she refused to return home, but he could not afford to maintain everything in Shanghai, so he and she each wrote letters to her mother, asking her to send someone to discuss the matter. The court declared that as a teacher, his marriage should require her mother's approval, and he should not engage in such improper behavior. The defendant said it was his great mistake and asked for leniency. Judge Jiang Shuzi, after beginning the debate, sentenced Wang Xiaohuai to one year of imprisonment, suspended for three years. Attorney Li abandoned the appeal, and Wang was released. The woman was taken back by her mother, Zhu Zhou.

Mother Sues Son for Theft 126

And Requests the Judge to Punish Severely

Result: Sentenced to Two Months of Imprisonment

Sun Xiangzi, a young man from Jiangbei, residing at No. 34, Dongxin Lane, Median Road, French Concession, is 22 years old this year. His original surname was He, and his given name was Yu Fu. Because his father died early, his mother remarried into the Sun family, and he changed his surname to Sun. After his mother married into the Sun family, she opened a brothel for a living. Xiangzi had already married and started a family. He used to work at the tram company, but because he did not seek advancement, he was dismissed by the company and became unemployed. He also liked to associate with hooligans. When he had no money to spend, he gradually stole household items such as clocks, candlesticks, bedding, and other miscellaneous items for pawn or sale. Because his mother's brothel was like an inn, she had many quilts, and over thirty of them were stolen. Recently, his mother, Sun Zhou, unable to bear it any longer, reported it to the French police, who sent detectives to arrest Sun Xiangzi, confiscating dozens of pawn tickets and recovering many stolen goods, all of which belonged to her. He was taken to the police station for detention. The day before yesterday, he was sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special Court. The police lawyer filed a lawsuit for theft under Article 337 of the Criminal Code. Subsequently, the plaintiff, Sun Zhou, testified that her unfilial son had stolen household bedding and pawned it for spending. She redeemed it, but it was stolen and pawned again countless times. Unable to bear it any longer, she reported it to the police and requested severe punishment. When questioned, Sun Xiangzi confessed that after he lost his job, he asked people to find him work, but he had no money for socializing. He asked his mother for money, but she refused, so he had no choice but to pawn the items for use. He claimed that taking his own belongings for pawn could not be considered theft. Now that his mother wanted to punish him, he could do nothing and requested severe punishment to please his mother. The plaintiff also stated that there were over a hundred pawn tickets for her son's stolen goods, but nearly a hundred had been destroyed, so not many stolen goods were recovered. She requested severe punishment to warn against unfilial behavior. After Judge Sun Peng examined the confessions and admonished the defendant, he immediately sentenced Sun Xiangzi to two months of imprisonment for continuous theft as a warning.

Armed Robbery Wounds Housewife 127

Chen Wu's Life in Danger

Chen Manzi, a native of Yangzhou, lives in the stove room at No. 1250, Siwen Lane, Datong Road, Xinzha Road. His wife, Wu, is his concubine and is 47 years old this year. At about 7 p.m. yesterday, three robbers dressed in blue cloth shirts and trousers suddenly broke into Wu's room, threatened her with guns, and forced her to take off the gold ring on her hand. Wu, upon seeing this, disregarded the danger and ran out, shouting for help in the alley. At that time, the robbers, seeing her escape, knew things were bad and also ran out. However, as she was shouting for help, residents gathered from all directions, and the robbers panicked. They pulled out their guns and fired two shots at her, hitting her head and shoulder, causing her to fall to the ground, bleeding profusely. The robbers then seized the opportunity to escape. Nearby patrol officers arrived, but they had already disappeared without a trace. They immediately reported to the police station and sent her to Guangren Hospital for treatment. An investigation into the gang was launched. However, as she was seriously injured, her life was in danger.

Establishment of a Pauper Loan Office in the Yangjing District of Pudong 128

The Yangjing District of Pudong has a large population, separated from Yangshupu by only a river. It has long been included in the urban area, and because of its low rent and convenient transportation to the bustling city, it is a gathering place for vendors. The area covers about twenty square li, with over 17,000 households and a population of over 70,000. The Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau's Pauper Loan Office, for the purpose of expansion, originally planned to establish another pauper loan office there. However, after investigation, it was found that local thugs were engaged in lending money at high interest rates, exploiting the poor. It is necessary to strictly crack down on this behavior, and the establishment of a loan office is even more urgent. Personnel have now been dispatched to liaise with the local party branch and public security sub-bureau, and it is expected to open soon.

However, because Detective Lang has refused to appear in court, the case remains unresolved. It has recently been learned from a certain source that since our Ministry of Foreign Affairs notified the relevant country's ambassador, ordering the Shanghai Municipal Council to immediately instruct the detective to surrender for the court to handle the case according to law, negotiations have made some progress. Mr. Zheng Jinwen, Founder of the Datong Music Society, Passed Away Yesterday Morning 130

Mr. Zheng Jinwen, Standing Committee Member and Director of Music Affairs of the Datong Music Society, was the founder of the society. He was gentle, humble, and amiable. He was exceptionally intelligent from a young age. At the age of twelve, he was proficient in silk and bamboo instruments. Later, he learned major musical pieces such as the pipa and zither. In his spare time, he explored musical classics and music theory, especially focusing on elegant ancient music. Mr. Zheng's achievements today were not accidental. In the past, he lamented the decline of Chinese music, believing that such a large ancient country was being criticized for having no music. He was deeply concerned and worried about this. Therefore, in 1925, he, along with Mr. Wang Tiyu, Wang Yuting, and Mr. Shi Liangcai, General Manager of Shen Bao, advocated the establishment of a music society to revitalize it. The plan was completed in less than a month, and Mr. Zheng was elected as the president. He strongly advocated using Datong as the society's name, believing that it was based on ancient and modern times, thoroughly researched, and created valuable music to meet the music of the world. This was Mr. Zheng's ambition. Later, he repeatedly led members to attend cultural gatherings and international gatherings to perform, which was highly praised by Chinese and foreign figures. The society was famous at home and abroad, and people from the party, government, and society gradually paid attention to it. In his spare time, Mr. Zheng also edited music books, among which "A History of Chinese Music" was the most brilliant. In 1930, the society was reformed, and a committee system was adopted. Mr. Li Shizeng, Cai Yuanpei, Chu Minyi, Wang Xiaolai, Zhang Gongquan, Zhang Yuejun, Feng Youwei, and other gentlemen sponsored and served as standing committee members, which accelerated the society's progress. Mr. Zheng was still not satisfied and strived for development, such as supervising craftsmen to imitate more than 160 kinds of ancient musical instruments, forming a large orchestra, composing large musical pieces, and so on. He spared no effort in training future generations. People in society hoped that he would achieve something, so that Chinese music could be placed in a bright position. However, heaven did not bless him, and the art star suddenly fell. Mr. Zheng suffered a stroke on the morning of the 23rd of this month. Medical treatment was ineffective, and he died of illness at 1 a.m. on the 24th, at the age of 64. The news of his death shocked the art world. Mr. Zheng had many students. Now, an organizing committee will be formed to assist in funeral affairs, and a request will be submitted to the committee to form a memorial service preparation committee to plan memorial activities to express sorrow.

Portrait of the Late Mr. Zheng Jinwen 131

Shao Jingfan, a Chinese detective from the Hongkou police station, learned that someone was selling narcotics, red pills, for profit at No. 31, Jiugeng Lane, Haining Road. Page 13

Fellow Merchants in the Straw Hat Export Business Organize a Association 133

Fellow merchants in the straw hat export business in this city operate businesses producing straw hats in the Ningbo, Shaoxing, and Taizhou regions, selling them overseas. Because there was no corresponding organization in the past, disputes and dishonored bills often occurred. It has recently been heard that over thirty businesses, such as Wang Xiangji, Huifeng, Shenyi, Wuzhou, Tongchun, Jufeng, Dalai, Shentai, and Zhang Junji, have initiated the organization of the Shanghai Straw Hat Export Business Association. The Shanghai Municipal Party Department has approved and registered the association, and issued Permit No. 399. Since receiving the permit, the association has begun preparations, electing Wang Jiuxiang, Zhang Shanhe, Feng Mingsheng, Shu Lincai, Zhan Baoqi, Xu Zhishang, Zhang Wenhuan, Shen Minli, and Lin Jinfu as preparation members responsible for the process. The temporary office is located at No. 5, Lane 1, Dean Lane. The association's declaration is recorded below: We, the straw hat export businesses from the Ningbo, Shaoxing, and Taizhou regions, specialize in exporting straw hats, selling them overseas, reaching tens of millions of dollars annually. However, due to the lack of corresponding connections and the organization of a association, everyone acts on their own, often leading to disputes, even manipulating the market, disrupting market prices, inciting female workers, and dishonoring bills. All of this can lead to bankruptcy for fellow merchants, let alone conducting foreign trade. Our country's famous silk and tea export industries have existed for over two thousand years, and their history is unparalleled by other industries. However, due to merchants adhering to old methods and the shortsightedness of seeking immediate gains, they have been seized and replaced by neighboring countries. Moreover, our industry's history is still young, and it is likely to follow in the footsteps of the silk and tea industries. In today's world of increasingly fierce commercial warfare, the survival of the fittest is the natural law. Looking at various European and American countries, their organizational steps for business are extremely strict, either monopolizing the market or aggressively dumping goods, competing openly and advancing steadily. The collapse of rural areas and the decline of industry and commerce in recent years have been long-standing issues, not accidental. Therefore, the prosperity or decline of an industry is extremely important for the livelihood of female workers and farmers. We, who are engaged in this industry, understand this deeply. In the face of the current crisis, how can we remain silent? Therefore, we have initiated the organization of the Shanghai Straw Hat Export Business Association, hoping to unite businesses and customers, dispel mutual barriers, strive for excellence in product technology, promote market expansion, and work together to save the situation. We hope that enthusiastic fellow merchants will actively join. The bright future depends on this. May our fellow merchants strive for this. We hereby announce our sincere intentions and hope you will understand. We hereby declare.

Yongmao Coal Yard Forced to Move Case 134

The Eighth District Branch of the Second Special District Municipal Association Resolves to Assist

The Yongmao Coal Yard at No. 94, Rue Coubert, French Concession, has been setting up coal depots on three vacant lots at No. 106 on the same street and Nos. 782 and 793, Rue de la Luta, for several years. They have always been at peace with each other. Recently, the Jiu Yi Real Estate Company, adjacent to the two depots at No. 106, Rue Coubert, and No. 793, Rue de la Luta, suddenly claimed that the two depots were damaging the company's properties, forcing Yongmao Coal Yard to move the two depots, otherwise, they would have to compensate for the loss of rent. Mr. Xu Shunbao, the owner of the yard, argued that the two depots had built high fences and stacked coal baskets near the bamboo fences before storing coal, so there was no risk of dampness or damage to Jiu Yi's properties. He politely refused, and the matter was shelved. Unexpectedly, on the 16th of this month, the French police suddenly sent Western police officers to the yard, ordering them to move all three depots within eight days and imposing a fine of fifteen foreign dollars. Yongmao Coal Yard is a member of the Eighth District Branch of the Second Special District Municipal Association. They reported the information and requested assistance from the Eighth District Branch. The branch held an emergency meeting at noon yesterday. Nine executive committee members, including Qian Kan, Cao Xianda, Wu Guowei, Zhang Zhiqin, Pan Dafu, and Ding Weisheng, were present. Wu Guowei was elected as the chairman, Zhou Guantian as the secretary, and the meeting was conducted according to regulations. First, Executive Committee Member Xu Shunbao reported the situation of being forced to move by Jiu Yi Real Estate Company and the French police. Chairman Wu reported that the association had sent letters to the French Municipal Council and the French Chief Inspector's Office, requesting them to consider the difficulties of merchants and exempt them from moving, but had not yet received a reply. After discussion, the following resolutions were made: (1) Report to the Second Special District Municipal Association and the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession, requesting practical assistance. (2) Send letters to major newspapers to publicize the inside story of the case, hoping to attract the attention of the public. (3) Send another letter to the French Chief Inspector's Office, requesting the revocation of the order to move. (4) Issue a declaration explaining Jiu Yi Real Estate Company's actions of pressuring Yongmao Coal Yard to move, requesting public opinion. (5) If necessary, take further action.

Verdict in the Case of a Vegetable Vendor Cutting His Wife and Her Paramour 137

Bai Lao Si Found Not Guilty

Bai Lao Si, a native of Anhui, 43 years old this year, has been engaged in selling vegetables. He lived with his wife, Zhou (30 years old this year, a native of Nanjing), and their eight-year-old son at No. 94, Route Mercier, French Concession. On January 9 of this year, at 3 a.m., Bai, as usual, went out to buy vegetables. When he returned home at 5 a.m. to sort them, he discovered that Li Zhijia, an acquaintance from his hometown (47 years old, residing at No. 6, Lane 128, Route de la Luta, guarding a self-flowing well at No. 159, Lane 1, Route Haig), was having intercourse with his wife, Zhou, in bed. Bai, consumed by jealousy, immediately used the bamboo pole used to carry vegetables to beat his wife and Li in bed. Unexpectedly, Zhou and Li resisted. In a panic, Bai used the sharp-edged knife used to sell vegetables to stab Li in the lower abdomen and Zhou in the arm. They shouted for help, and the sub-landlord heard the noise and reported it to the police. Detective Xu Jinlong rushed to the scene and arrested Bai, along with the murder weapon, and took them to the police station for detention. The next day, the police sent Bai to the Second Special Court, charging him with attempted murder and detaining him pending further investigation after the injured parties recovered. This has been previously reported. Later, Li and Bai Zhou recovered from their injuries and were discharged from the hospital. Judge Zhang Chaozuo of the Second Special Court held a continued hearing. The police changed the indictment, charging Bai with the crime of assault under the Criminal Code. The interrogation has been completed. The day before yesterday, Judge Zhang presided over the First Criminal Court, ordered the defendant to be brought to court, and acquitted Bai Lao Si. During the appeal period, the defendant was detained in the detention center awaiting instructions.

Record of the Sha Dai Guild's Executive Committee Meeting Yesterday 142
