Free Talk

Style and Genius 149

— Leng Mo

Although what is presented here are two old terms, there is no intention of exploring their true meaning from their elusive word meanings. Style and genius obviously each represent one aspect of Chinese literature, and they seem to be opposed to each other in any setting. These two can be broadly used to represent two schools in Chinese literature. After style and genius clearly became school names and resisted each other, a third school of Shenyun (神韵, divine rhyme) appeared, but that was just a popular compromise that was ultimately completely ignored, so Shenyun is not a term that can be a match for the former two. On the other hand, as the literal meaning of Shenyun suggests, Shen (神, divine) is an expansion of genius, and Yun (韵, rhyme) is a reduction of style. As a result, it did not receive sympathy from the genius school, and the style school similarly despised it, and its compromise and reconciliation were not very successful.

Recently, a group of people advocated the literature of the late Ming Dynasty. There is no doubt that they want to stand on the side of the genius school. But they recognized that the opponent standing on the opposite side was the Fangjinqi (方巾气, square cap spirit) and Daoxuepai (道学派, school of morality), then they seem to not be very clear about their own sect. The literature of the late Ming Dynasty cannot be directly opposed to Daoxue, but it stands in the circle of thought of the late Ming Dynasty and consciously breaks out of the circle of thought of the Song Dynasty. The Chan crown of the late Ming Dynasty thought worn by the literature of the late Ming Dynasty is actually more conspicuous than the square cap of the Song Dynasty Daoxue worn by Song literature. If we do not distinguish between literature in a broad sense and literature in a narrow sense, the texts of the Song people defending Daoxue are indeed larger in quantity. But those literatures should be listed as pure philosophy and not included in literature. If we only take pure literature such as prose and poetry of the Song Dynasty to compare with the prose and poetry of the late Ming Dynasty, then the authors in the literature of the late Ming Dynasty can't forget to express their thoughts (expressing their aspirations) everywhere, while all in the Song literature is just a kind of atmosphere cultivated through Daoxue, and rarely directly gives reasoning in pure literature.

If we use words such as "zhi zhong he" (致中和, achieving balance) and "fa er jie zhong jie" (发而皆中节, issuing and all are moderate) to explain that kind of atmosphere, then it is obvious that what is created in literature should be style. And it is natural for the style school to cite Song Dynasty literature. There is no problem that a literature contains philosophical thoughts. The only question is how harmonious the degree of integration is. Style can be said to be a sign of the degree of integration. This is also the basic difference between the style school and the genius school. The genius school does not talk about integration but requires nakedness.

The so-called nakedness is the meaning of nakedly expressing their genius or expressing their aspirations that they advocate. But whether aspiration is innate and needs to be expressed nakedly is indeed a question. I am afraid that being able to reach that state still depends on cultivation. What is human nature at all? This question really can't get any answers. Becoming a saint and absolute saint is actually equally difficult. The models of Confucius, Mencius, Lao Tzu, and Zhuangzi are equally difficult to imitate. However, the outline of the model of Confucius and Mencius is more accurate, while the model of Lao Tzu and Zhuangzi varies greatly under various lights. It is easy to recognize whether something compared to the correct outline is similar or not. On the contrary, it is okay to say whether it is similar or not. The followers of Lao Tzu and Zhuangzi can forget their own depravity and blame the followers of Confucius and Mencius for depravity, so it is also natural.

But here, let's not involve pure ideological issues yet. On the one hand, wearing a square cap that advocates the doctrine of the mean and promotes the methods of being human, and on the other hand, being an expressionist school in literature, the relationship between them can be reluctantly separated, but in other respects, the style school can also be regarded as the same as the Fangjinqi. I know what genius and style are, and they are not worth talking about now, but since some people are re-evaluating genius, at least style should be taken care of.

Random Talks on Historical Anecdotes (4) 150

— Cao Juren

Su Dongpo said: "Articles are everywhere, only a skillful hand can pick them up." When first reading history books, those major events and major figures attract our attention. If we follow this path, we will have to write dull textbook-style historical texts. After reading for a long time, lovely events and lovely figures flash out here and there. The great figures, heroes, and sages in our eyes are still living people made of skin and bones, flesh and blood, just like us, with emotions, reason, a bright side, and a dark side. We put aside the front and enter from the side, put aside the big things and enter from the small things, and our writing will be very active. The story of mankind written by the great modern American historian Vna Leon (Vna　Lcon), I was stunned to read when I first saw it. When he wrote about the French Revolution, I put down the book and wondered how he would write about Napoleon because others used hundreds of thousands of words to write about Napoleon and still felt it was not enough. How could he cover it with thousands of words? When I turned it over, he wrote:

"I am now sitting in front of a very comfortable table, the table is full of books, one of my eyes is looking at my typewriter, one eye is looking at my cat, and I am telling you that Emperor Napoleon is not worthy of being human. But if I look up slightly and see countless cars and horses suddenly stop on the street outside the window, and a burst of drums in my ears, and the short and capable Napoleon comes riding on a white horse wearing a worn blue military uniform, then I will not be able to control myself. I am afraid I will also throw away my books, abandon my cat, leave my home, abandon everything, and run after him, and he can lead me wherever he wants. My grandfather followed him like this, and God knows that he was not born a hero. And thousands of other people's ancestors also followed him like this. They did not get any rewards, nor did they hope to get any rewards. They were willing to sacrifice their limbs and lives to be driven by him, leaving their hometowns and traveling thousands of miles to the fortresses of Russia, England, Spain, Italy, or Austria, calmly watching the continuous artillery fire and death battle... (The Story of Mankind, Volume 2, page 172)

The way he wrote it, although it was a branch and a section, was enough to set off the center of gravity of the event and the soul of the figure, and all of them were used as themes. Then, for "one twenty-four histories", are we still afraid of finishing writing it? Often read the Historical Records and the Book of Han, and see Sima Qian and Ban Gu record the affairs of Emperor Gaozu of Han, with many extravagant and exaggerated places. But from the lines, such as:

(1) Mother Ao should rest by the Great Lake, and dreamed of encountering a god; at that time, there was thunder and lightning and darkness, and his father Taigong went to see it, and saw Jiaolong on it, and soon became pregnant, and then gave birth to Emperor Gaozu.

(2) Emperor Gaozu was a person who loved wine and sex, and often drank and lay drunk from Wang Ao and Wu Fu Huangjiu, and Wu Fu Wang Ao saw that there was always a monster on it. Emperor Gaozu bought wine every time and stayed to drink, and the enemy doubled. When he saw the monster, at the end of the year, these two families often folded their debts and abandoned their responsibilities.

(3) Lu Gong was good at judging people, and saw the appearance of Emperor Gaozu, so he respected him and invited him to sit in the seat. After the wine was over, Lu Gong said: I have been good at judging people since I was young; I have judged many people, but none is as good as Ji, I hope Ji will cherish himself!

(4) Empress Lu lived in Huizhong with her two sons, and an old father passed by and said to the queen: Madam is a noble person in the world... Emperor Gaozu chased him and asked the old father, and the old father said: The appearance of the king is so noble that it cannot be said. ... When Emperor Gaozu was rich, he did not know where the old father was.

(5) Emperor Gaozu was drunk and walked through the Ze in the middle of the night, ordering one person to walk in front; the one who walked in front threw back and said: There is a big snake in front of the path, I wish to return. Emperor Gaozu drunk said: What is the fear of a strong man! Then he drew his sword and cut the snake. ... Later people came to run to where the snake was, and there was an old woman crying at night,... My son said that the emperor is also a son, and now the son of the Red Emperor cuts the son,... The woman suddenly disappeared. ... Emperor Gaozu was happy and proud.

(6) Emperor Gaozu was hidden in the Mangyu Mountain Ze, and Empress Lu and others often found it. Emperor Gaozu asked strangely, and Empress Lu said: Where Ji lives, there is often a cloud of gas above. ... Emperor Gaozu was also happy.

Those sections all have traces of the Liu and Lu families colluding to create rumors, as long as they are interspersed, they can be written into an interesting sketch. Also, such as Xijing Zaji, remember:

"The Supreme Emperor moved to Chang'an, living in a deep palace, sad and unhappy. Emperor Gaozu secretly asked the left and right about the reason, because his favorite in his life were all butcher young people, buying wine, selling cakes, fighting chickens, and playing Cuju, and he missed this; now there is nothing like this, so he is unhappy. Emperor Gaozu then made Xinfeng and moved all the old friends to it; the Supreme Emperor was pleased. Therefore, Xinfeng has many ruffians and no children of clothing and hats, so it is also. When Emperor Gaozu was young, he often sacrificed to the Fen Yu Society; when he moved to Xinfeng, he also re-established it. Emperor Gaozu had built Xinfeng and moved the old community lanes, buildings, and objects to the old state; the men and women, old and young, carried their heads on the road, and each knew their room, released dogs, sheep, chickens and ducks on the main road, and also competed to know their homes. The craftsman Hu Kuanying also managed it." It is also an excellent theme.

Little White Mountain 151

— Xicun

Crossing the Wender River and heading south along the Songhua River, the road is no longer a flat road but a country road. Dust is flying on the road, and the five grains are standing in the fields waving to you, as if to say:

"City people, what are you doing in the countryside?"

The weeping willows along the way have long recognized the people who come to play, and they understand:

"These people are here to go sightseeing at Xiaobaishan."

The road is gradually moving away from the river, which means it is gradually approaching the side of the mountain.

Xiaobaishan is not big, probably because of this, it got the nickname "Little" on Baishan? It is an isolated mountain, with no mountain ranges connected to it. Even so, the mountain itself still has two small mountain peaks. It is not too high either. Looking at it from Jilin City from afar, it looks like a pile of earth.

Here, there is not a bit of the meaning of the city. You will see the boundless fields of green wheat, clumps of forest bushes, and when you see the crooked farmhouse thatched cottages and the simple and loyal farmers, you almost think that this is a place of quiet, and it will immediately arouse your aversion to the city and the city people.

The mountains are forested with tall oak trees, short mountain old red trees, and tender willows. The forest is like putting a velvet coat on the mountain. As for the grass and miscellaneous flowers, they are the patterns on the velvet coat.

As soon as you enter the mountain pass, there is a deer circle, and people who come here must stop. The wooden circle is badly damaged and has been in disrepair for many years. People play with the deer for a while, and then go up the mountain along the narrow winding path.

There is a temple on Xishanfeng Mountain, a desolate mountain ancient temple, which has always been mutually used in famous places in China, and no one can do without the other. It seems that the name of the mountain is due to the temple, and the temple must be built in a famous mountain to be considered enough face.

There is a hall in the temple, and a large plaque is hung horizontally under the antique eaves. The hall is very wide, and there are no walls on the east and west sides, and the walls are mostly open. On the gable walls hang plaques written by generals and other figures from the Qianqing period, all of which are exaggerated words of beautiful scenery. If you take the words in the plaque too seriously and lose yourself, you will definitely be disappointed in the scenery in front of you. Honestly, Xiaobaishan doesn't have any scenery, but people want to go around, and I don't know what the reason is.

However, when you leave the open hall of the temple and climb to the east mountain peak, you will not feel very happy. Looking south, what first comes into your eyes is a white belt, like a white snake, but when it winds to the east side of the mountain, it is the lovely Songhua River. Then, you will feel admiration for the distant mountains; they present several colors in front of you, and for that kind of erratic smoke, you will think of the story of the "mirage". Then you look at Jilin City in the northeast. The city is surrounded by mountains, setting off a depression in the middle. To say it madly, the surrounding mountains are like the side of a small boat, and Jilin City is just a pile of rotten goods in the boat. Yes, the houses in Jilin are all old and dilapidated. But when your eyes turn to Baibailong, the mood that your eyes receive is different. There, brand-new high-rise buildings, red brick and bluestone, there are three or four of them, standing tall in the green fields, ferocious. This is the Jilin University campus. Left attached, the station building of the Baibailong Terminal on Ji-Hai Road is also a noteworthy building, which is three-dimensional, and it seems that some people have said that it is German style. The railway extends from the front of the station, one towards the southwest and one towards the northeast. This was originally a village on the edge of the city, but now it has become lively.

Listening to the birds chirping on Xiaobaishan is an interesting thing. As long as you can calm down, you can hear many different kinds of bird languages, and you can also see many different shapes and feathers. If you are not a hunter and do not carry a shotgun, they will also land in front of you and chat with you, telling each other's short and long stories.

Knocking 152

— Chen Yumen

Heavy footsteps hesitantly stepped onto the stone steps, peeking through the door crack to see if the dog was out. Dark, thick fingers touched the door and gently knocked, a hoarse voice uttering a trembling sound.

The child hid behind, sniffling, breathing warm air into their sleeve, knowing there was a doorbell in the center of the door, but knocking on the door was enough to cause a moment of fear.

A sorrowful and kind expression was put on the face, eyes fixed on the two door panels, hoping to visit several more houses in a day, meeting charitable people who cared for the old and pitied the poor.

Perhaps a cane could ward off enemies, knocking on the door could relieve the hunger that twisted the intestines, but the sharp wind laughed at the holes in the tattered clothes, and the closed door seemed to carry a cold arrogance.

Letter (Part 1) 153

— Xingwen

Although spring has not yet arrived, the sound of rain is already a bit weary. Spring rain falls slowly. The sound of raindrops outside the window corresponds to the beating of the heart in my chest. Gently pressing the letter against my chest, the up and down movement of blood in my heart is felt by my hand through this letter. If the soul is in the heart, it must now be happily flying into this letter. I smile slightly, smiling at this poor and lovely soul, smiling at its happiness.

The electric light illuminates the entire room in the evening. The light appears particularly gentle, with a milky white hue. The light shines on my smiling face, and the light also knows that I am happy. The sound of rain falls drop by drop, seemingly knowing some secrets in my letter. I feel like I want to immediately buy an image of Guanyin Bodhisattva to hang up. I am willing to burn the purest and finest ambergris in front of her image and worship. It must be the inspiration of Guanyin Bodhisattva that brought me this letter, which is filled with the aura of immortals and the flavor of Buddha. The words seem to have been soaked in the fragrant dew of plum blossoms before being taken out.

I thank Guanyin Bodhisattva for her greatness, she has given me this kind of comfort. I feel as if I am lying in a cradle made of soft swan feathers, sleeping freely and without worry in the spring air and sunlight, filled with a faint scent of wine and pink hues. When I wake up, there are songs like light pearls and floating jade flying all around, the songs flying and often brushing against my face.

From today onwards, I feel the preciousness of life, and I begin to feel a warm willingness towards my rosy future. I begin to see swallows and orioles fluttering in the "bright future" ahead. It seems as if there are lazy flowing waters, and white gulls and snow egrets are gently floating on the water. I tell God that I am willing, a hundred million times willing, to abide by the words in the letter. I will definitely fulfill my career as she hopes, and I believe I have the ability and opportunity. I feel like I am paddling hard on the calm, green spring water. I have already seen the village under the green trees ahead, that corner of the red building, the embroidered windows, and the person I have dreamed of waiting by the window.

Towards Evening (6) 154

— Qu Yi

Room number thirteen of the Dahan Company has a hundred-candlepower electric light, shining brightly and illuminating all the furnishings in the room.

The room is horizontally long. The windows face the Dahan Company's balcony. A long sofa is placed by the window. At the entrance, two sofa chairs flank a tea table with a thick glass top. A clean heated bed is靠inside: Outside the heated bed, there is a round doorway with a dragon pattern, with a white gauze curtain hanging low outside the doorway, half-opened. Separated from this heated bed by a slat wall is the bathroom. Outside the bathroom, there is also a copper bed lying horizontally, also covered neatly with a white gauze curtain; the red silk quilt, somewhat sexually stimulating, is folded靠inside the bed. A printed white blanket emits a white light, as if secretly mocking the despicable behavior of people.

The walls of the room are pure white, and under the illumination of the electric light, the entire room overflows with snow. The wind outside the window blows in with the smell of coal smoke, but in this white light, it adds a sense of coolness to people. At this time, the owner of the room, Hu Yiyuan, is lying on the heated bed, writing his "successful article."

In the middle of the heated bed is a mahogany plate. In the center of the plate is a ghostly-fire-like opium lamp. Next to the opium lamp are some silver boxes filled with opium paste. Hu Yiyuan, lying on his left side, is holding a pipe in his right hand and an opium needle in his left hand, packing the opium. A big man with a potbelly is lying on his right side.

The light from the opium lamp is flickering as if in a panic. Like a snake's tongue, it often stretches out from the round hole at the bottom of the cover, licking and cauterizing the opium paste on the pipe. Hu Yiyuan is also very clever in playing with this snake-tongue-like light. When the snake's tongue really wraps around the opium paste and emits a burst of flames, he immediately uses his thumb and forefinger to pinch the opium paste, extinguishing the flames; and pinches the opium paste into a small, round ball. At the same time, a bone-penetrating fragrance emanates from between his fingers, causing his throat to reflexively swallow a mouthful of saliva. He burns and pinches it like this three or four times until he finally uses the opium needle to make a small hole in the opium head, and a pipe of opium is packed. Hu Yiyuan begins to suck on it, making "chi ge chi ge" sounds.

Sports News

Illegal Dissolution Case of the Far Eastern Athletic Association 155

Meeting of the International Olympic Committee

Will be Proposed for Resolution Today in Oslo

Secretary Baetes Has Already Sent a Letter to Shen Siliang

Since the Far Eastern Athletic Association (FEAA) was illegally dissolved by Japan and the Philippines during the 10th Far Eastern Games last year, the Chinese National Amateur Athletic Federation has appealed to the International Olympic Committee for a fair resolution, as the Far Eastern Athletic Association is affiliated with the International Olympic Committee. Now, the International Olympic Committee has scheduled an important meeting to be held today in Oslo, the capital of Norway. Dr. Wang Rutang, a member of the Chinese Olympic Committee, is unable to attend due to unforeseen circumstances. However, according to Shen Siliang, the general secretary of the National Athletic Federation, Secretary Baetes of the International Olympic Committee has sent a letter to Shen, stating that the illegal dissolution of the Far Eastern Athletic Association by Japan and the Philippines has been accepted and will be brought up for discussion at today's meeting, and a fair resolution is expected. As for the location of the 12th World Olympic Games, it will also be decided at today's meeting.

The Chinese Team Won the Right to the Finals in Yesterday's Semifinals of the International Football Tournament 156

A Decisive Victory Over Russia by Twelve to One

Will Hold the Finals with Portugal

In the Western Union Football Club's International Cup football match, China and Russia held their semifinals in Shenyuan yesterday afternoon. China eliminated Russia with a huge score of twelve to one and won the right to the finals, which will be held with Portugal at a later date. With the thriving image of Portugal this season, the Sino-Portuguese finals will be very interesting to watch. Yesterday's game was completely one-sided. The Shaguer team represented Russia in the game, and the difference in strength was so great that China had complete control. More than 4,000 spectators burst out laughing. Li Yichen scored eight goals alone, but the Chinese team's performance was not yet at its best.

China Painstakingly Scores Four Goals in a Row

China kicked off and immediately took the offensive. About seven minutes into the game, Wanxiang Hua crossed from the side, Luo Haiguang jumped up and headed the ball. The Russian goalkeeper got the ball but lost it again. Li Yichen rushed up and kicked the ball into the net. Although the five Russian forwards tried their best to counterattack, the Jiang and Li defenders were heavily guarded and ultimately could not enter. Once, Li Yichen received a ball in the penalty area and was about to shoot forcefully when the Russian left inside defender panicked and mistakenly committed a handball, resulting in a penalty kick. Li Yichen scored with one shot. Then, Jia Youliang dribbled straight in, kicked the ball with great force at a suitable position. But the goalkeeper dived to catch the ball. Jia and Li charged forward to dribble the ball and the man, and when they sent it into the net, Sun Jinshun dribbled deep. The Russian goalkeeper ran out to block, Sun immediately passed to Li Yichen, who was able to calmly score into the empty net, leading by four goals.

The Russian Team Bravely Recaptures a Goal

The Russian defenders, ashamed of their previous dereliction of duty, blamed themselves and fought back with extra effort. Ten minutes before the end of the first half, the Russian center forward went straight in alone and shot a ball from outside the penalty area, hitting the target and making it four to one. After that, they fought back and forth several times, desperately fighting. In the chaos, the first half ended, with the Chinese team leading by four to one.

China's Victory Makes Up a Dozen

Less than two minutes after the break, Wanxiang Hua got the ball and picked it up. Li Yichen made no mistake. At this point, the Russian team was already at the end of its rope. It could not counterattack and found it difficult to defend. The Chinese team's defensive skills were particularly outstanding. Li Yichen was especially brave and scored two more goals in a row, making the score seven to one. Before long, Luo Haiguang scored with the help of Yichen, and Li Yichen then scored again (eight to one). The Chinese team became more and more courageous and their offensive power never wavered. In the last five minutes, Sun Jinshun scored twice, and Luo Haiguang got a penalty kick and scored again, making it a dozen. Before the center kick-off, time ran out, and the Chinese team won with an overwhelming score of twelve to one.

The Russian Team

Jiangda Sports Association Suspends Basketball Competition Next Month 162

The Competition Schedule Will Be Decided in Shanghai in the Coming Days

The Venue Will Still Be Divided Between Shanghai and Nanjing

The Jiangda Sports Association will successively hold basketball, volleyball, track and field, and other competitions starting next month. The association had originally planned to convene a meeting in Shanghai recently, but because there were no particularly important matters, it has switched to using communication methods to discuss everything. A reporter from the Daily News learned the following from the person in charge of the association:

The Meeting Was Suspended and Discussion Was Conducted Through Communication

According to the discussion, the Jiangda Sports Association had originally planned to convene a meeting in Shanghai recently to discuss the various championship competitions that should be held this semester. Now, in addition to sending letters to the various organizing committees to prepare, there is no need to convene a meeting, so it has switched to using communication methods to discuss everything. A few days ago, it sent a letter from Shanghai to Mr. Xu Shaowu, a member of the association in Beijing, and Mr. Wu Demao Duan Naxun to discuss track and field matters, because these three are responsible for preparing the Jiangda track and field competitions. In addition, regarding the eligibility of athletes, whether students who graduate in three and a half years can participate, please also discuss with Mr. Wu Yunrui. According to the latest regulations of the Ministry of Education, universities should graduate in four years, and those who can graduate in three and a half years are no longer applicable today, so this case should not be discussed.

Basketball Competition is Actively Underway

As for the various championship competitions that should be held this semester, there are three items: basketball, volleyball, and track and field. The association has previously decided that the basketball competition will be held in March, the volleyball competition will be held in April, and the track and field competition will be held in May, all of which must be completed within that month. Currently, the Jiangda basketball competition is actively underway and is scheduled to begin in early or mid-March. The competition schedule will be decided in Shanghai in the coming days. The competition venue will still be divided between Shanghai and Nanjing as usual. At that time, the basketball teams of Fudan and Guanghua will first go to Beijing to compete against Jinling and Zhongda, and then Jinda and Zhongda will come to Shanghai to compete with Jinan and Chizhi.

Education News

Ministry of Education Orders on Improvement Points for Vocational Education in Hubei 168

The Ministry of Education recently issued an order to the Hubei Education Department, instructing them to follow the improvement points for vocational education in Hubei Province as detailed in the previous inspection report by Inspector Gu Zhaolin. It is understood that vocational schools in Hubei Province, after being urged and reorganized by the Education Department, have generally shown gradual progress. However, regarding the establishment of departments, the department should comprehensively plan based on the province's industrial and social needs, and stipulate the distribution areas and the number of departments to be established in schools to ensure that supply and demand are aligned. In terms of equipment, many schools throughout the province are still poorly equipped. The existing equipment of various engineering vocational schools should be enriched as soon as possible, and newly established provincial and district agricultural vocational schools should pay more attention to completeness. Furthermore, connections should be made with vocational circles to provide students with more internship opportunities. Regarding curriculum, the teaching material outlines promulgated by the ministry should be followed, striving for practicality, correcting the accumulation of empty talk and raising standards. Vocational guidance should be earnestly implemented to prevent students from misidentifying goals and changing careers or pursuing further education midway. In addition, private vocational schools in Hubei Province have not been developed. The Education Department should provide awards and assistance within its capabilities to promote progress. The points that need to be improved are detailed as follows:

(1) The implementation plan for reorganizing Hubei provincial secondary schools proposed by the Education Department is generally suitable. However, there is considerable duplication in the departments established in the current vocational schools. The Education Department should comprehensively plan and allocate appropriately, preventing schools from creating their own trends and hindering unified design.

(2) The current vocational education situation in Hubei Province, except for agriculture, where provincial schools are being planned and district schools are being established separately, is mostly focused on engineering. Among them, only one or two schools have a basic level of equipment, and there are many places where supplements are needed. A phased method for supplementing equipment should be stipulated according to the actual situation of each school, based on the lowest standard, to gradually improve.

(3) Engineering vocational schools must strive to enrich their factory settings and actively promote their connections with vocational circles. For example, according to the relevant responsible personnel of the Jiang'an Machine and Engineering Plants under the Pinghan Railway, "No vocational school students have ever come to the factory for internships, and vocational schools in Hunan and Hubei provinces have not contacted the factory. Occasionally, vocational school graduates seek work, but they are generally difficult to approve due to their poor experience. However, students' knowledge is far superior to that of workers. If mechanical engineering graduates are willing to come to the factory as interns without being restricted to specific positions, then they will be easier to promote and have better prospects than workers after they have achieved some results in their internships. Currently, newly graduated vocational school students seeking work either demand high salaries or are unwilling to work hard, which makes the factory dare not ask. This is not without reason." It seems that school personnel pay little attention to the matter of graduates interning at factories. Indeed, such matters of connecting with vocational circles are inherently cumbersome and difficult to implement in the mainland, and may be beyond the ability of one or two schools to manage. It is best for schools to jointly handle them and request assistance from the provincial government, education department, and construction department at any time. (4) The printing and copperplate departments of provincial vocational schools have a good foundation of equipment and have achieved effective results. Missing or lacking parts should be supplemented as soon as possible to achieve completeness. The applied chemistry department has some confidence in the tung oil industry and pigment experiments, so it should increase its research component and establish a small-scale factory for practical training to specialize and refine skills. It can also establish contact with Zhijiang Vocational School in Hunan Province, which has the same subject, for reference. (5) The original mechanical engineering and dyeing and weaving departments of the Third Provincial Secondary School have good factory equipment, but they are all old equipment from many years ago, and there have been few additions recently. The content of the factory and various machines lack organization. Attention should be paid to it and the teacher should guide the students. Practical training should also take into account technical issues to ensure students have expertise and specialization. The applied chemistry department should also narrow its scope to avoid being too broad. Since papermaking is said to be more certain and factory equipment funds are secured, a thorough investigation should be conducted on all aspects before setting up a factory for trial operation.

(6) Since the Second Provincial Secondary School merged into one school, the school affairs have been reorganized and are organized, but students have too few opportunities for practical training outside of classroom lectures, and training is also lacking. The school's proposed plan to establish a bank should be carried out as soon as possible. Labor training for students should also be implemented to ensure students are proficient in technology and can endure hardship.

(7) The dyeing and weaving department of the Provincial Girls' Vocational School has good equipment but still requires some necessary supplements, which can be added in phases. The home economics and embroidery departments should establish cooperatives, imitating the common practice of Hunan women's vocational schools, to benefit students' practical training and enhance their vocational awareness. Teachers should also create new designs and pay attention to the composition of goods in students' practical works, instead of just imitating popular products on the market to avoid a loss of creative meaning. Patterns, diagrams, flower designs, and sample chapters should be collected and organized into volumes for reference in learning.

(8) The municipal vocational school is composed of three schools divided into three locations, which are far apart, making management very inconvenient. Before the new school buildings are built, a setting plan should be determined and the subjects to be established should be planned properly. New students should be suspended and classes reduced to ensure the establishment of vocational subjects with perfect equipment, practical training, teaching, and training so that some achievements can be made. The current curriculum in each class should not strive for deep and advanced content. Textbooks must be suitable for students' levels. For example, using university textbooks for bookkeeping in senior commercial subjects is called improvement, but it has no practical benefit. More internship opportunities should be provided for senior commercial students to avoid being too broad and to correct the previous fallacy of preparing solely for further education. Although the original commercial subjects are based on the viewpoint of the Wuhan commercial market and there is a need to continue operating, the Second Provincial Secondary School has also set up a commercial subject, which is a dual-track system. Most of its graduates are also employed in Wuhan, Yangxia, and Hanyang. It is questionable whether the commercial market can accommodate three or four classes of graduates each year. Therefore, the establishment of the school's subjects should be planned in consultation with the provincial schools in a comprehensive way to be appropriate. Among the two branch schools, the girls' department is better organized, but students' vocational awareness is still not clear and must be corrected.

Surveying Confucius' Tomb and Temple for Repairs 169

Regarding the repair of Confucius' tomb and temple, the Executive Yuan ordered personnel from the Ministry of Interior (Chief of Section Tang Wencong) and the Ministry of Education (Chief of Section Zhong Lingxiu) to meet, together with experts in ancient architecture such as Liang Sicheng, to go to Shandong to inspect and estimate costs. Tang, Zhong, Liang, and Mo (Mo Zongjiang is Liang's assistant) arrived in Jinan on the 16th and 17th respectively. As it was Sunday, they began on the 18th to meet with engineers and surveyors from the provincial government's Civil Affairs, Education, and Construction Departments, eight people in total (12 total), to go to Qufu to survey Confucius' tomb and temple. The Confucius Temple covers dozens of acres and has a majestic appearance. After the officials inspected the temple, such as the Dacheng Hall, which is eighty or ninety feet high, scaffolding was erected to inspect the upper layer. The roof leaks and needs major engineering. The surrounding walls and column bases also need to be repaired. The Wenkui Hall (the name of the hall is unknown, whether it is Kui Xing Hall or Da Kui Hall, the reporter did not ask clearly and did not record it) is ten feet high. All parts of the roof also need to be repaired. In addition, Yan Zeng Meng and the Yansheng Gong Mansion have been inspected. Comparatively speaking, the Confucius Temple project is larger. Confucius' tomb covers dozens of miles. Except for the tombs of Confucius, Zisi, etc., which are concentrated in one place, the tombs of Confucius' descendants surround it on all sides, numbering in the millions. Ancient trees line the way, and pine and cypress forests are everywhere (pine, cypress, and juniper trees are the most numerous). It is heard that in recent years, a Mr. Zhang from Anhui donated more than 30,000 yuan to repair Confucius' tomb, so Confucius' tomb has been slightly reorganized and is inferior to the Confucius Temple. The officials stayed in Lu for five or six days. Engineering expert Liang Sicheng made a plan and instructed his assistant Mo Zongjiang to work with the technicians from the provincial government to conduct a detailed survey. Liang returned to Peiping because of matters in Peiping, and then joined another commissioner to work with Mr. Mo and others to carry out surveying and design work. The two chiefs of section, Tang and Zhong, returned to Beijing on the 23rd. Liang, an engineering expert, plans to draw detailed charts and tables based on the results of the inspection and survey, and to create a description of the types of materials needed for the project and all plans. In about two weeks, the representatives of the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education will meet with relevant personnel from Shandong Province to discuss the estimate of the project and the construction method. After the representatives of the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education have a concrete plan for their second visit to Shandong, the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education will submit the estimated engineering expenses to the Executive Yuan for approval.

Central Research Institute of Zoology and Botany to Investigate Coastal Fish Production 176

To Proceed in Four Phases, Scheduled to be Completed in Four Years

First Phase of Work Determined to Depart in Mid-April

The Central Research Institute of Zoology and Botany, in view of the large output of fish in our country, in order to understand the situation of coastal fish production, has organized a Chinese Coastal Fish Production Investigation Group, which is scheduled to depart in mid-April. The details are described as follows:

Reasons for Initiation The Central Research Institute of Zoology and Botany, recently, in view of the large output of fish production in our country, and the nature, types, producing areas, fish feed, etc., have not been studied in detail. Also, because our country's fishing industry is declining, in order to promote revitalization and understand the situation of coastal fish production, last year, Wu Xianwen was sent to Yantai, Shandong, for investigation. At that time, due to the short time, the results obtained were very small. Therefore, it has now been decided to organize a Chinese Coastal Fish Production Investigation Group to conduct large-scale searches and, incidentally, to test seawater properties, temperature, etc., as a reference for the development of fish production.

Work Plan The work plan is divided into four phases, each lasting one year, and is expected to be completed in four years. The first phase of the work will be from Qinhuangdao, Hebei, to Chengshanjiao, Shandong. The second phase of the work will be from Chengshanjiao to the Yangtze River Estuary. The third phase of the work will be from the Yangtze River Estuary to Shantou. The fourth phase of the work will be from Shantou to Guangdong Bay. Currently, the first phase of the work plan has divided the section into three areas, each with twelve fishing stations to facilitate investigation.

Organizational Overview The organization of the group is headed by Wu Xianwen, a researcher at the institute. In addition, there are two assistant members, several testers, and several fishermen. In addition, there is a fisherman leader. It has been agreed with the Navy Department that a warship will be allocated for use at that time. In addition to conducting fishery surveys, the first phase of the work will also focus on testing plankton.

Scheduled Departure The first phase of the investigation is scheduled to depart in mid-April. The budget for the expenses is more than 40,000 yuan. In addition to the 10,000 yuan extracted from the institute's annual expenses, the remaining insufficient amount will be submitted to the government for subsidy. The original four-year work plan may be shortened to two years if difficulties are encountered in terms of funding.

German Far East Association Donates Huge Amounts of Equipment to Tongji University 179

Overview of Health Education in the Wuxi Huibei Experimental Zone 183

— Yang Xieli

Jiangsu Provincial Education Institute established the Huibei People's Education Experimental Zone in the Fifth Autonomous Region of Wuxi County in order to provide students with practical training in popular education. Since its establishment, it has been more than two years, and it has achieved considerable results in various aspects of people's education. The business area has also gradually expanded. There are now six branch areas in the entire area, all equipped with offices, and a total of 29 staff members. The area under its jurisdiction is 91 square li, with 106 villages, 5,381 households, and a population of 32,405, of which agriculture is the most popular occupation, accounting for 61%. This is the general situation in this area.

Health education is one of the key experimental items in this area. This article will only focus on the current situation of this education business, and describe it in detail:

(1) Disease Treatment

A simple pharmacy is set up in each area, storing more than 20 kinds of common medicines. Intern students serve as doctors and train students in public schools to use the pharmacy. The registration fee is two copper coins, and follow-up visits are free of charge. Medicines are charged at cost. The number of patients seen, based on statistics from May 1st to the end of October of this year, a total of five months, was 1,578 males and 2,382 females. The types of diseases were mostly skin diseases, accounting for 48% of the total, malaria accounting for 28.16%, eye diseases accounting for 19.34%, and other diseases accounting for 4.5%.

(2) Vaccination of Smallpox

This year, 695 people have been vaccinated against smallpox in this area, and it is still in the process of being vaccinated. The methods are: (1) using public school weekly meetings, tea garden talks, family visits and wall newspaper propaganda to publicize the importance of vaccination, (2) holding registration, (3) starting vaccination, charging three copper coins per person.

(3) Public health

(1) Eliminating open-air latrines——The methods are (1) propaganda, (2) talking with local leaders, (3) investigation, (4) individual persuasion, (5) joint implementation with the public. In October of this year, a total of 56 open-air latrines were eliminated in Chenjiaqiao in this area.

(2) Setting up trash cans——First discover the need for setting up, and then assist the township office in handling it. In mid-September of this year, a total of 26 trash cans were set up in Hengjie Township in this area. The accumulated garbage is collected by farmers and used as fertilizer.

(4) National Martial Arts Group

The area invites boxers to perform in various places, sparking the public's interest in national martial arts. At the same time, enrollment advertisements are posted and registration is held, and then training begins. There are now two national martial arts groups with a total of 88 members.

(5) Sports Field

The area uses wasteland to open up four sports fields, each equipped with simple sports equipment, totaling four horizontal bars, two parallel bars, one slide, and one stone shoulder. In addition, there are two football fields, one basketball court, and one sand pit. The expenses are borne by the local area, and local people are jointly responsible for guidance and management. There are now organizations and training of various ball teams, and a public sports meeting will be held regularly. (End)

Annoying Whooping Cough (Part 2) 185

— Zhong Zhihe

(2) Spasmodic Stage. Mostly without fever. If fever occurs, it is often accompanied by complications. This stage has a unique spasmodic paroxysmal cough. Each paroxysm consists of fifteen to twenty continuous coughs, short and painful. After all the inhaled air is coughed out, a sudden deep breath is taken, accompanied by a crowing sound. The "Whoop" is just this one inhalation, and then the continuous paroxysmal cough starts again. This happens several times, and the child's face suddenly turns purple. If children with this disease are together, one child's cough often triggers the others to cough in response. However, after the cough stops, the child still plays normally, as if without any suffering. In severe cases of paroxysmal cough, the jugular veins are distended, and the eyeballs bulge out. Nasal discharge and tears flow, the conjunctiva is congested, and the eyelids and face become swollen. In very severe cases, hemiplegia may occur. Towards the end of a paroxysm, vomiting of food often occurs. In severe cases, blood may be coughed up from the nose. Involuntary urination and defecation are commonly seen. This type of cough is more severe at night. Children have difficulty ingesting food, leading to nutritional deficiencies and emaciation. Small gray ulcers appear on the frenulum of the tongue. The frequency of paroxysms varies; in mild cases, it occurs about five or six times a day, while in severe cases, it occurs about every half hour. If it occurs repeatedly more than a hundred times a day, it is often fatal.

(3) Recovery Stage. The disease gradually subsides. The frequency of paroxysms gradually decreases. There may still be symptoms of bronchitis during this period.

Complications... Other diseases often complicate the course of whooping cough. Bronchopneumonia is a common and often fatal complication, accounting for perhaps two-thirds of the mortality rate. Spasms are also common during the course of the illness.

Treatment Methods... (1) During a whooping cough epidemic, special attention should be paid to prevent children from being infected. If a child in a family has the disease, strict isolation should be implemented to prevent transmission. It is even better to move healthy children to an area where the disease is not present. (2) Taking the patient to the seaside is a suitable convalescent area. Going to the countryside in summer is highly recommended. In general, it is most important to have little dust, plenty of trees, and fresh air. Patients with severe symptoms should rest quietly in a large bedroom. Patients with mild symptoms and a fever below 37.5 degrees Celsius can spend more time outdoors absorbing fresh air. It is advisable to sleep with the windows open at night, but avoid drafts. (3) Sunbathing is very beneficial, especially from 8 to 10 am, as this is when there is more ultraviolet light, which has bactericidal properties. (4) The temperature in the sickroom should not exceed 100 degrees Fahrenheit. The air should not be too dry. Methods should be used to sprinkle water in the room or hang wet sheets in the room. It is best to have water vapor in the room. A kettle can be placed on a brazier to boil water and produce water vapor. (5) The vomit and sputum of the sick child should be spat into a spittoon and strictly disinfected. It is even better to burn the sputum if it is spat into paper. (6) During the catarrhal stage, bed rest is necessary. Feed liquids. If it is an infant, dilute the milk. Prevent catching a cold. (7) Choose nutritious foods, such as malt extract, milk, milk powder, and glucose. Feed every two to three hours. If vomiting occurs immediately after eating, feed again. Avoid dry, powdery foods as they can irritate and easily cause coughing. Foods containing Vitamin D are especially good. (8) Clothing should be loose and warm; flannel is especially suitable. Keep warm and avoid getting cold again to prevent complications such as bronchopneumonia. (9) Using an abdominal support belt can prevent paroxysmal vomiting and provide comfort, as the abdominal muscles contract violently during paroxysmal coughs, compressing the full stomach and causing vomiting. (10) Hot water baths or sitz baths are good. (11) Consult a specialist to administer artificial sunlamp irradiation, relying on the effects of ultraviolet light to assist the patient's body. (12) Camphor oil can be applied to the chest daily, but caution should be taken to avoid burns or injury to the skin. (13) Consult a doctor for medication and bacterial lysate injections.

Pain Relief in Medicine (Part 3) 186

— Li Xing

The Basic Principles of Pain Relief

This article describes the academic aspects of pain relief in scientific medicine. It is unlike the common practice of simply taking a painkiller tablet when one feels pain, without considering the cause of the pain, the nature of the medication, or how the pain relief works. The science of pain relief is indeed scientific medicine. First, it seeks to identify the cause of the pain. Second, it determines how to prevent the pain beforehand. Third, it assesses the suitability of local or nerve anesthesia. Fourth, it decides whether to use medication for pain relief or to use non-medication methods. If medication is used, it is necessary to understand what kind of medicine to use, why to use a particular medicine, what the medicine does within the body, and whether it is ultimately beneficial or harmful; what benefits and harms it has.

Many medications and surgical procedures for pain relief have been invented. When used properly, pain can be eliminated and overall health can be improved. When used improperly, temporary pain relief can be achieved, but at great expense to overall health. Here, I will briefly describe the principles of pain relief in medicine for the reader's study.

(1) Physiological Principles of Pain Relief: As stated at the beginning of this article, pain is caused when nerve receptors in the injured or problematic area transmit sensations to the brain via the spinal cord and brain pathways. The overall perception of pain resides in the brain, not in the injured or problematic area. Therefore, according to physiological principles, the following methods can be used to relieve pain: (1) Numbing or eliminating the sensory function of the receptors at the site of injury can stop the pain. (2) Numbing the nerve pathways to prevent transmission of sensations can also relieve pain. Local injection of anesthetics for pain relief works on this principle. Furthermore, performing anesthesia within the spinal canal can also eliminate pain. For example, injecting anesthetic into the spinal cord can eliminate pain from the abdomen down. Another method, commonly used and often misused, is to use narcotics to cloud the brain, making it unaware of pain, thereby supposedly relieving it. In reality, the pain and the underlying problem remain. When used appropriately, this method can be a temporary lifesaver in times of extreme suffering. However, when used inappropriately, it can be a source of great harm. The harmful effects of opium, morphine, and other strong narcotics stem from the improper use of pain relief methods.

(2) Understanding the Cause of Pain: In medical practice, although doctors immediately seek to relieve a patient's pain, they should not simply administer anesthetics to numb the brain without understanding the cause. Instead, they should rapidly identify the cause of the pain and then implement appropriate pain relief methods. Relieving pain with knowledge of the cause is conscious and targeted. Relieving pain without knowing the cause is unconscious and untargeted, and can sometimes be harmful. It is important to recognize that pain in the body can sometimes signal an emergency situation, requiring prompt and appropriate intervention to prevent life-threatening consequences. This is the guiding principle for pain relief in all surgical cases. Not only for severe pain, but also for common pain, one should first understand the cause and then use appropriate methods for relief. For example, a student may have headaches from reading too much due to nearsightedness. Another person may have headaches due to constipation. Yet another person may have headaches due to typhoid fever. And another person may have headaches due to syphilis. It is clear that using a single anesthetic or painkiller tablet to treat all these headaches is irrational. Therefore, thoroughly investigating the cause of any pain before implementing suitable pain relief methods is the modern approach in this age of scientific advancement.

(3) Pain Relief Without Harming the Body: In urgent cases of pain, the primary concern is obviously to relieve the pain immediately. However, one should not rely solely on taking or injecting painkillers for the sake of expediency. One should pay attention to using methods that do not harm the body, and may even improve health. As long as the science of pain relief is understood and applied properly, this is not a difficult task.

Modern medicine has revealed that frequent use of many pain relievers is harmful to the body. There are also many pain relief methods or surgeries that are beneficial and harmless to the body. Therefore, one should first choose those that are beneficial to the body. This knowledge of choice must be sought within genuine medical science. (To be continued)

Common Sense About Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eye Hygiene 187

— Tang Renzhen

(36) The Reason Why Eyes Can See

Two small eyeballs can accompany a person throughout their life, constantly providing all the necessary images. What ingenious, exquisite, and lovely little organs they are! We should protect them with utmost care. The method of protection is to focus on their hygiene. I have already published articles on eye hygiene in this journal. Now I would like to discuss the reasons why they can see. Perhaps readers can develop an even greater love for them because of the complexity of their structure and the ingenuity of their physiology. Before I discuss the reason why eyes can see, I must first discuss the structure of the eye and its physiological functions, which will make it easier to understand.

1. Structure of the Eye: The main part of the eye is the eyeball. The eyeball is composed of a membranous sac and the contents within the sac. It is connected to the brain via the optic nerve. A small portion of the front of the membranous sac is completely transparent, while the rest is opaque. This membranous sac is formed from three layers of membranes, namely the outer membrane, the middle membrane, and the inner membrane.

(1) Outer Membrane - also known as the fibrous coat of the eye. The transparent part of this membrane at the front is called the cornea (Figure 1) (commonly known as the "black of the eye"). The opaque part at the back is called the sclera (Figure 2) (commonly known as the "white of the eye").

(2) Middle Membrane - also known as the choroid. This membrane can be divided into two parts, the anterior part being the ciliary body (Figure 3) and the iris (Figure 4), and the posterior part being the choroid proper (Figure 5).

(3) Inner Membrane - also known as the nervous membrane, which is the retina (Figure 6). This membrane is where the optic nerve (Figure 7) is distributed.

As for the contents within the sac, there are three types: the lens (Figure 8), the aqueous humor (Figure 9), and the vitreous humor (Figure 10). (Please refer to the attached diagram).

(1) Cornea (2) Sclera (3) Ciliary Body (4) Iris (5) Choroid (6) Retina (7) Optic Nerve (8) Lens (9) Aqueous Humor (10) Vitreous Humor (11) Ciliary Muscle

2. Physiological Function of the Eye: When discussing the physiological function of the eye, it is useful to use a camera as an analogy. The diaphragm of a camera is like the iris of the eye. Their functions are exactly the same. When we take photos, the diaphragm is narrowed in strong light and widened in weak light. Therefore, the pupil (the pupil is a small hole surrounded by the iris) usually shrinks when viewing objects in strong sunlight and dilates when viewing objects in the dark. The principle is the same. The converging lens is equivalent to the lens of the eye. Because the lens is rich in the power of refracting light, the dry plate is equivalent to the retina of the eye (To be continued)

Hermaphrodites 188

— Jiang Hongli

The definition of a hermaphrodite is an individual possessing both male and female reproductive organs.

Hermaphrodites are divided into "true hermaphrodites" and "pseudo-hermaphrodites." A true hermaphrodite is an individual who not only possesses both male and female reproductive organs but also has both male and female reproductive functions. According to embryology, this type of hermaphrodite should not exist.

A pseudo-hermaphrodite has external genitalia that appear to be of both sexes, but the gonads are either testes or ovaries. Those with testes are called "male pseudo-hermaphrodites," and those with ovaries are called "female pseudo-hermaphrodites."

(1) Male Pseudo-Hermaphrodites: (Androgynoide) Account for three-quarters of the total. Their original sex is male, but the penis is small, resembling a woman's clitoris. The scrotum is not fused on both sides, resembling a woman's labia. At the same time, hypospadias is present, resembling a woman's vulva. Because the scrotum is incompletely developed, the testes are often hidden in the abdomen.

(2) Female Pseudo-Hermaphrodites: (gynandroide) Their original sex is female, but the clitoris is abnormally enlarged and protrudes like a male penis, capable of sexual intercourse. Parts of the left and right labia are fused together, resembling a male scrotum. If the ovaries descend into the labia, they are even more similar to male genitalia.

These two types of pseudo-hermaphrodites often undergo special physiological changes due to environmental factors or sexual activity. For example, male pseudo-hermaphrodites often associate with women, and over time, their behavior and thoughts become more feminine. Their bodies also undergo changes, such as a delicate voice, a slender waist, long sideburns and arched eyebrows, enlarged breasts, and wide hips, with fully developed curves in all parts of the body. The most peculiar thing is that the genitals sometimes ooze blood, but this blood should not be mistaken for menstruation, as it is mostly caused by bleeding from sexual intercourse injuries.

Female pseudo-hermaphrodites live and interact with men daily, their lifestyles are the same as men, so their bodies become developed and strong, their muscles protrude, and soon they also have a rough appearance.

In medical history, there is a record of a woman named Mary, who lived to be eighty-four years old. She had always been the head of her household, but after her death, an autopsy revealed that she was originally a male.

Another person married a wife for six years. One day, a doctor accidentally discovered that his wife was originally a male. However, because their love was so strong, they could not bear to part despite this great shock. From then on, they continued their homosexual love life as if nothing had happened.

In summary, pseudo-hermaphrodites are caused by abnormal or deformed embryonic physiological development, similar to cleft lip infants or imperforate anus. People lacking medical knowledge often believe that the birth of a hermaphrodite is the result of sins committed in a previous life. The parents of hermaphrodite children often consider them to be unlucky, so they often abandon them. However, after detailed explanation, this absurd prejudice should be eliminated!

A Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (42) 189

— Hu Jiayan

Chapter 9 Clinical Course

B. What is meant by mid-field infiltration? The origin of this term is related to X-ray examinations. For the convenience of examination, the left and right lungs are divided into three parts, namely the upper, middle, and lower fields. This is different from the usual anatomical division of lung lobes. The middle field includes the area below the second rib and above the fifth rib. This area includes parts of both the upper and middle lobes of the lung (speaking only of the right side). According to past theories, the initial site of pulmonary tuberculosis was limited to the area within the lung apex. Now we know that this is not the case. It is located in a part close to the underside of the collarbone, and on the surface of the lung. This state is medically termed independent infiltration. Its location is within the scope of the mid-field, so this type also has the specific names "mid-field infiltration" or "mid-field tuberculosis." Its clinical symptoms are not numerous. Generally, the onset is somewhat acute, with conditions similar to those of influenza. Coughing and excessive phlegm will be discovered later. Although the amount of sputum is not large, tubercle bacilli can sometimes be detected. The percussion sound is weaker, and the breath sounds have slight changes at the branch of the trachea, but sometimes physical examination yields no results. The temperature sometimes decreases. Although the disease is progressing, the general condition is sometimes very good, and there is no difference from normal people. The most powerful proof of this aspect is, of course, thanks to the X-ray examination procedure! In most cases, the infiltrated part shrinks and hardens, resulting in recovery. In other cases, caseous degeneration causes liquefaction, resulting in the development of early cavities. In still other cases, extreme spread to the entire lobe of the lung results in caseous pneumonia, which has the worst prognosis, but ultimately accounts for a very small proportion.

C. The term apical tuberculosis was very popular in the past, but it is definitely not the initial site of the lesion. According to recent evidence, most cases are due to the atrophy of mid-field tuberculosis and its transfer to the lung apex. Therefore, this type is secondary and progresses through the lymphatic or vascular system. Its course is mostly chronic, and clinically, it also has a latent state, with no significant symptoms. Unless the area of infiltration is very large, the continued spread of the tracheal branches and vascular system is possible. (End of this chapter, to be continued)
