Shenbao Local Supplement Movie Special

Hollywood's Special School that Emphasizes the Three Aspects of Education and Simultaneously Imparts Intellectual Power (Part 1) 217

— Zhu Jiabo

Hollywood has a special school called the Carl Gurtis School for Boys and Girls. The educational policy there does not advocate any particular system, but the purity of its purpose, the perfection of its methods, and the excellence of its achievements are indeed worthy of attention by educators in general. Therefore, we will record all of its contents below in detail for the reference of those who are concerned.

That school is located between Culver City and Hollywood, on a grand scale. It is a place where the children of Hollywood movie stars receive knowledge, temper their muscles and bones, and cultivate their morals. That school is not an ordinary school, but a place that every child, regardless of gender, dreams of every day. There, swimming and boxing are also part of the curriculum. Outdoor sports occupy the same important position as English and arithmetic.

Almost ten years ago, Hollywood's famous director Cecil B. DeMille and other big stars, such as Jack Holt, Will Rogers, and Noah Beery, planned to establish a school with the late physical education expert Carl Gurtis and educator Brabant, to develop children's physical and mental strength in parallel. They greatly agreed with that plan and first sent their own children to the school they founded. This is the beginning of the current Carl Gurtis School.

In smaller cities, or those with established scales, almost no one dares to propose the establishment of such a reformist school. But in Hollywood, which was in its early stages of development at that time, they felt that this plan was very much in line with theory, so they proceeded without hesitation. Sure enough, after only one year, the students' parents were amazed by their children's achievements.

In that school, even kindergarten students practice swimming. When they enter elementary school, they are taught foreign literature. Physical defects can be corrected by exercise. A temperament that is just and gloomy can be transformed into kindness and happiness. The increase in weight, general health, and mental agility of each child are all considered to be remarkable achievements, which has led many movie stars who are parents to send their children to that special school. Even powerful families who do not work in the film industry want to send their children there. However, due to limitations in location and equipment, the school authorities have maintained the original enrollment of eighty students.

The faith and praise of Hollywood film industry figures for the school can be proven by the words of Clive Brook. Clive Brook's daughter Faith and his son Clive Jr. both attend that school. He said: "The best lessons these two children get there. But good lessons are available in other schools as well. What I approve of as a special feature of this school is that it gives every child the physical skills that make them grow up without being attacked by disease and losing or diminishing the joy of life. They not only educate children's minds but also train their muscles and bones. If a little child knows how to swim, ride a horse, skate, play tennis, and play golf, they will have fewer opportunities to feel lonely or uneasy in the future."

Clive is right. If a person's body and mind have been trained in the same way, his life will be very balanced and full of interest.

That is the firm theory of the current principal, Brabant, the ideal that more than a dozen teachers at Carl Gurtis School share, and what has been tested and proven by major educators for more than a decade, that increasing children's physical strength can greatly promote the development of knowledge. Brabant is able to confirm this ideal with student records, because 80% of the students at Carl Gurtis School who go on to ordinary elementary or secondary schools are able to advance one to three grades in each subject.

Now, let us describe the general situation of an ideal student from the admission procedure to the initial training at the school. For example, let's say the student's name is Jimmy. His mother is a female star. This five-year-old Jimmy is the treasure in his mother's eyes, more precious than a contract with a company. One day, she took Jimmy to see Principal Brabant. She received a plain reception from the school authorities, as if they didn't know she was a very popular female star, which made her a little angry.

If the eighty student slots have not yet been filled, she will receive a blank certificate to check her physical condition, and her husband will be asked to have her family doctor fill it out item by item and submit it within two or three days, along with knowledge and psychological tests. And if she doesn't mind the plain reception from the school authorities after she goes back, which is usually not the case, she will definitely bring Jimmy back to that school again in two or three days. (To be continued)

Germany to Convene International Film Conference in Late April 218

— Fu

The Soviet Film Association initiated an international film exhibition in Moscow in February of this year, and invited film industries in the Far East, Europe, and the Americas to send representatives and selected works to participate in the exhibition. After receiving the invitation from the Soviet authorities, our country collected representative works from major companies and sent them for exhibition. Those who went to participate from the Shanghai film industry included Zhou Jianyun, manager of the Mingxing Company, and movie star Hu Die.

According to a Berlin telegraphic dispatch on February 21, the German government also intends to convene an international film conference of the same nature in Berlin in late April, and has telegraphed various European, American, and Far Eastern countries that produce and show films, inviting them to participate. The invitation has been issued by the German Central Film Bureau, and the dates are set from April 25 to May 1.

According to news released by the German Film Bureau, the number of representatives dispatched by various countries, not including the national representatives, is approximately 800. In addition, if we add the national representatives, such as the representatives of the annual meeting of the German National Film Association, etc., then the gathering of global film industry celebrities, experts, and movie stars in Berlin will exceed 1,500, which can be said to be a grand occasion, perhaps exceeding the Soviet film exhibition.

Furthermore, most of the representatives from distant countries who have gone to Moscow to participate in the Soviet Union's international film exhibition will tour major scenic spots in Western Europe and the West after the closing of the exhibition, and then attend the World Film Conference in Berlin in late April, which will be a win-win situation and will not cost much.

It is not the first time that Germany has convened an international film conference. The last World Film Conference was also convened by Germany, held in Berlin in 1928.

Praise for "Diary of a Virgin" 219

— Yunmen

The most dashing and elegant leading man, Robert Montgomery, has consistently maintained his graceful, generous, and relaxed strengths since his performances in "The Anonymous Mr.," "Forsaking All Others," and most recently, "The Last of Mrs. Cheyney." However, Robert will lose his love twice in his latest work, "The Old Testament and the New Covenant," due to his optimistic personality. But this is a story for later, so let's not mention it for now. Now, "The Diary of a Virgin," which is currently being screened in "Nanjing," features Robert Montgomery and the talented Anne Harding in a second collaboration. "The Diary of a Virgin" is the most popular work in the life of the American playwright N.S. Behman. It was performed continuously for eight months in the Broadway Theatre in New York, which shows its great appeal. If we observe the attitude of the American newspapers' comments, we should also have the idea that it is difficult to have another good play, and at the same time, it is also enough to prove its value on the screen. The following are some of the American newspapers' comments:

New York American—"The Diary of a Virgin" is really more than just a wonderful play. Of course, it is one of the most successful and least numerous works of this year.

New York Times—This is truly Behman's most mature masterpiece declaring human nature. It is as lofty as the sky and as deep as the sea.

Daily News—Although "The Diary of a Virgin" is a complicated comedy, the individual personalities of the characters in the play have been vividly portrayed by Behman, making it an interesting and wonderful product. Undoubtedly, it should be listed as a "must-see."

New York Evening Post—Writing with a pen, it is very insightful. Behman's observation of all kinds of life here can be said to be exploring the subtleties.

World-Telegram—For this "Diary," I can only use two words to criticize it. Those are "adult" and "temptation." (The meaning of these two words is particularly ambiguous)

Anna Sten's Husband Who Will Also Devote Himself to the Screen 220

— Donglin

It is said that Anna Sten's husband, Dr. Eugene Frenke, will become a new film artist in Hollywood in the near future.

The wife of this Russian movie star, Falek, was an architect in Russia, so apart from doing a little film script with his wife after coming to Hollywood, it can be said that he has no experience in the film industry at all. But he always wanted to do something in the film industry, and he finally did it.

He wanted to be a director himself, but he had no experience, so naturally no producer was willing to give him a chance to try. Therefore, he began to look for a very attractive story. It just so happened that at that time, Dr. Cornish, a famous scientist in California, succeeded in reviving a dead dog.

This is what Falek needed. Wouldn't it be extremely appealing to film this wonder of the new era? So he began to write an interesting film script about this great discovery. Then he obtained permission from Dr. Cornish to borrow the film of his experimental results when filming in the future.

After everything was done, he went to Lamel, the boss of Universal Company, to discuss filming this film. Lamel agreed to him, but stipulated that the film could only be produced at a very low cost.

This film, "Life Returns," has now been completed. At the same time, Falek also proved that he did have extraordinary directing talent. Although it only took eleven days and there were no big stars in the cast, people who have seen it said that "Life Returns" is a rare and interesting film recently.

Falek said to reporters in a confident tone: "Now I can work in the film industry with my wife. We often work together very well and with a lot of understanding. So I believe we will definitely be able to do something meaningful in Hollywood."

Movie Novel

The Schoolteacher's Loving Mother (Grand Old Girl) (1) 222

An American production by Ai Kai Hua Lei Dian Hua Company, starring Mei Lao Bo Xun

Some people go through life without ever knowing the meaning of the word "failure." This trait is possessed by Miss Lulan Beiersifu. However, Lulan Beiersifu's struggle is not for herself, but for her many young students. Lulan Beiersifu has been the principal of the Municipal Middle School in Afang Tai'er for twenty-eight years. Although she feels physically and mentally exhausted after these long years, she secretly finds solace in reminiscing about her past achievements. She herself can't recall how many times she made up her mind to fight for her "children," for their physical, intellectual, and moral well-being, for their right to choose their own entertainment, and for the foundation of their future lives.

She is now alone, sitting at her desk in the principal's office, pondering a new struggle that has recently arisen. She is not a fool. She knows that her opponents are combining forces to deal with her personally. She knows that regardless of the outcome of this struggle, she will pay an immense price. She knows that she has no other path to choose. Her weary eyes—her intelligent, kind, and understanding eyes—unconsciously focused on a wooden plaque hanging on the wall. It was a gift from the graduating class of 1906, with a line branded on it: "Do what is right—that is courage."

Looking at it, she couldn't help but feel a surge of joy. Courage... righteousness... indeed, she possessed both of these qualities. Let it be whatever Joseph Jielai, the most powerful man in the area, rich with money and the owner of a newspaper in Afang Tai'er, may say. She knew that his inexhaustible wealth had many dishonest and incomplete sources. She knew why Kelalunsi Daide, the gambling den of Kelike Daide, could remain open permanently. She knew that there were many sycophants in the area, echoers who agreed to everything, and many local "political thugs" who wanted to lick sores and suck pus, hoping to get a share of the leftovers. Thinking about this, she frequently shook her head. She bit her own lip. Even the local school inspector, Helunte, came to her personally to warn her not to be too enthusiastic and to use some "diplomatic means."

Helunte said to her, "Miss Beiersi, in any case, Daide has already invested a lot..." Beiersi immediately retorted, "Invested? It seems to me that it is a harm to the area, the creation of evil forces. Daide's gambling den is not a place for my children to gather." Helunte narrowed his eyes into slits, looking at her maliciously, and asked, "What evidence do you have?" Miss Beiersi glared and said, "I have no evidence. But as long as I am alive, I will find it one day!"

Indeed, she had obtained evidence... She sighed softly, thinking of... but not complaining about the price she had paid and the failures she had experienced. She clenched her teeth and made up her mind to achieve the final victory. Why were they so foolish? They didn't know that what she cared about most was Jili Jielai, the orphaned daughter of Joseph Jielai. Jili was a senior in high school, beautiful in appearance but spoiled and headstrong, and always a leader among her classmates. Jili thought that going to Daide's place was a bold and interesting thing to do. There was an ice cream counter there, which seemed perfectly harmless on the outside. But behind the ice cream counter, there was a "back room," where Kelike Daide sold special drinks. Daide also lured a group of young people into gambling.

One day, Miss Beiersi wanted to reason with Daide herself. He had once been her student. But now Daide knew that he had a protective charm and was not afraid of what an old woman could do. He laughed at her. But he still liked her. Everyone couldn't help but like her. But now, Miss Beiersi saw Daide's arrogance and knew that her authority as principal no longer reached this former student. She had no other choice but to fight him. (To be continued)
